Venice Palace: British-Italian Talks Begin, Disapproves of Compromise with Germany, Italy's Position Largely the Same as France 21

(Rome) British Minister Without Portfolio Eden, after coming from Paris to Italy, arrived here at 7:00 PM tonight. Italian Deputy Foreign Minister Suvich and Prime Minister Mussolini's chief secretary Aloisi personally welcomed him. Eden is scheduled to begin talks with Prime Minister Mussolini at 10:00 AM tomorrow morning. (Havas dispatch on the 23rd)

(Rome) British Minister Without Portfolio Eden and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini held their first talks this morning at the Venice Palace for two and a half hours. Deputy Foreign Minister Suvich, Mussolini's chief secretary Aloisi, and British Ambassador to Italy Drummond were also present. As for whether the talks achieved concrete results, people here are skeptical. According to the Italian government spokesperson, Eden could not explain the justification for Britain's actions regarding the Anglo-German naval agreement. As for the Sky Treaty issue, it is more related to Britain and less related to Italy. All the issues raised by Britain were requests to Italy, while Italy is in a defensive position. Italy's firm attitude is generally regarded as evidence of the close friendship between France and Italy. The government spokesperson also said that the Abyssinian issue is not within the scope of the British-Italian talks. The rumors that Eden proposed a plan advocating intervention by a third country to seek a friendly solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute are also untrue. (Havas dispatch on the 24th)

(Rome) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and Eden will discuss the naval issue this morning, or also the Western Sky Treaty and the Danube Conference. It is expected that the Italian Prime Minister will express the same position as France regarding the Anglo-German naval agreement. However, according to Italian newspapers, although Italy criticizes Britain's unilateral actions and disapproves of the method of compromise with Germany used by Britain, it is satisfied with the Anglo-German treaty. Italian officials are not prepared to discuss the Abyssinian issue unless Eden presents specific suggestions from the British government in order to resolve this dispute. The Italian Foreign Ministry spokesperson stated today that even if the Abyssinian issue is raised for discussion, Eden may not have satisfactory suggestions. Italy's attitude can also be seen in this statement. The spokesperson rejected the talk of territorial and commercial concessions, saying that unless there is action to ensure that Abyssinia will no longer harm Italy, Italy cannot and will not withdraw its troops stationed in the territory. The spokesperson also stated that the Italian-Abyssinian conciliation committee, which is scheduled to meet in The Hague tomorrow, does not have the power to resolve the main points of contention between the two countries. (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

(Rome) British Minister Without Portfolio Eden, after winning a diplomatic victory in Paris, dispelling France's doubts about the Anglo-German naval agreement, arrived here from France last night. Italian officials welcomed him as usual. Those who greeted him at the station included Deputy Foreign Minister Suvich, Italian representative to the League of Nations Aloisi, and British Ambassador to Italy Drummond. The talks between Eden and Mussolini will begin today, and if necessary, will continue tomorrow. It is believed that in addition to the naval issue, Britain and Italy will also consider the Western Sky Treaty and the Danube Conference. According to officials here, the Abyssinian issue will not be discussed, but it is believed that this matter may not be completely avoided. It is generally hoped that Eden's visit to Rome will further strengthen the solidarity expressed by Britain, France, and Italy in Stresa. The unilateral act of Britain concluding a naval agreement with Germany has indeed surprised people here, but the Italian government seems to understand Britain's act of compromise with Germany. At the same time, the French ambassador to Italy visited French Prime Minister Laval in Paris and rushed back to Rome on Sunday night, and visited Suvich yesterday morning for consultations. This is a sign of close cooperation between France and Italy due to Eden's mission. (Reuters dispatch on the 24th)

Britain Wishes to Mediate, Maintain Peace in East Africa, British Newspaper Reports Eden Prepares to Make Suggestions, Allow Italy to Build Roads and Trade Rights 22

(London) According to the Daily Mail, Minister Without Portfolio Eden will propose to the Italian authorities on the Abyssinian issue during his visit to Italy that Britain will fully assist Italy to satisfy Italy's "legitimate demands in Abyssinia" in exchange for a guarantee that Italy will not take military aggression against Abyssinia. The so-called legitimate demands are the right of Italy to build a railway, which passes through Abyssinian territory to connect the Italian territories of Eritrea and Somaliland, the right to use certain water sources and pastures in the Ogaden area of Abyssinia, and the right to develop Limen enterprises in northern Abyssinia. All these rights have been stipulated in the treaty on Abyssinia signed by Britain, France, and Italy in 1906. Moreover, the Anglo-Italian agreement in 1925 also recognized the area where the railway will be built in Abyssinia in the future as the sphere of Italian influence. In addition, it is rumored that Britain has allowed Abyssinia to designate a sea passage in British Somaliland for Abyssinia to use to compensate for the rights that the country has ceded to Italy. Although this statement has not been confirmed, the newspaper believes that it is possible. (Havas dispatch on the 24th)

(Paris) Although it is generally said that British Minister Without Portfolio Eden will discuss the Anglo-German naval agreement and the Locarno Pact, the "Newspaper" said that the Abyssinian issue will also be discussed, because one of those accompanying Eden to Rome is a Mr. Dion Bombsen, who is a British expert on North Africa and Egypt issues. It is heard that Britain will not spare any cost to maintain peace in East Africa. Britain will probably allow Abyssinia to use the ports along the coast of British Somaliland, and Abyssinia will use a part of its territory for Italian colonization, allow Italy to have trade privileges in Abyssinia, and be able to build a railway that passes purely through Abyssinian territory to connect the Italian ports of Mar Brava and Mogadishu as an exchange condition. (Havas dispatch on the 24th)

Anglo-German Agreement Lays the Cornerstone of the European Situation, German Representative Issues Talk on the Eve of Departure, Advocates Cooperation Between Britain, France, and Germany 24

(London) German representative General Ribbentrop left for Germany today. On the eve of his departure, he met with a Reuters diplomatic reporter. Ribbentrop said that the disarmament issue has been discussed for many years, and the Anglo-German naval agreement is the first real success and the first step towards arms limitation. He meant that Europe had made a mistake and has not yet been corrected, that is, trying to solve various problems of various countries at the same time. Because of this agreement between Britain and Germany, there will be no more naval competition, and we have broken the ice in the European political situation, opening the way to solve other problems. Therefore, the agreement may become a cornerstone of Europe's true stability. Germany firmly believes that Europe bears the mission of the entire civilized world. As for the rumors that Germany intends to alienate Britain and France, they are all lies. This is not the spirit before the flood, but a repetition of the mistakes before the Great War. If we want to see the revival of Western Europe, we must think and believe in a grand strategy. It is said that he takes assisting in the close unity between Britain, France, and Germany as his life's career. This is true. Other European countries will be happy to join this kind of unity. He feels that we are now on the right path. (Reuters dispatch on the 23rd)

Report to the Head of State

London Issues Communiqué

(London) Anglo-German naval talks have ended. The Foreign Office issued the following communiqué today: Since the exchange of notes on June 18, Britain and Germany have continued to discuss naval issues. The attitude of both sides is the same as in previous talks with other governments. Both sides have thoroughly exchanged views on the future restrictions and the extent of naval construction. Germany's views and the British government's proposal to conclude a general naval agreement in the future will be notified to the representatives of the countries concerned in future talks. It goes without saying that the exchange of views between the British and German governments is only of a temporary nature, because the final decision depends on the attitude of other countries in the future international naval conference. (National Telegram on the 22nd)

Agreed Points Between Britain and Germany

(London) The Daily Express reported that in the Anglo-German naval treaty, Germany agreed never to use submarines to attack merchant ships. Regarding this point, German leader Hitler will issue a declaration in the near future. Britain and Germany have mutually agreed that the two countries' warship construction programs will not be implemented quickly. Germany's warship construction program will be completed by 1942. As for Britain adding new ships to replace old ships, because the Washington Naval Treaty is still valid, it must wait until 1937 to begin construction. The construction project will be extended for several years. The newly-built battleships will not be put into use until 1943. As for the maximum tonnage of submarines, Britain and Germany have agreed to be between 600 and 800 tons. (Havas telegram on the 24th)

Anglo-German Naval Agreement: The United States Neither Approves Nor Disapproves; Limiting Capital Ships Violates Original American Stance; British Measures Merely Exacerbate Japanese Arrogance 26

(Washington) The British Ambassador to the United States, Lindsay, notified the American government the day before yesterday with a copy of the Anglo-German naval agreement and detailed information about the negotiations. At that time, Deputy Secretary of State Phillips only expressed to the British Ambassador the hope that this agreement could pave the way for universal limitations on naval armaments. He did not express any opinion on the content of the Anglo-German naval agreement. Outside rumors that the US government considered the Anglo-German naval agreement acceptable were denied by the State Department. In short, the US government has not expressed approval or opposition to the Anglo-German naval agreement. This attitude accurately reflects the general public opinion in the United States. The general consensus is that the Anglo-German naval agreement is the most surprising diplomatic development since the war. According to some, while the European air force issue has nothing to do with the United States, any issue concerning the naval ratios of countries around the world is considered by the United States to be directly related to itself. Now, without consulting the United States in advance, Britain has simply changed the German naval system stipulated by treaties through bilateral negotiations. It should be noted that this naval system is not only stipulated by the Treaty of Versailles but also by the US-German peace treaty. Moreover, the United States seeks to maintain naval parity with Britain. The establishment of the Anglo-German naval agreement not only affects the naval policies of France and Italy, but also has a significant impact on the total tonnage of the British Navy. The United States will not turn a blind eye to this. Britain has already decided to build twenty new cruisers in the near future, and rumors are circulating that it will also need to build ten capital ships. After the British general election, there is deep concern that the British government will use Germany's construction of the latest type of fleet as an excuse to implement a large-scale naval construction program. If that is the case, the American shipbuilding program will inevitably be affected. Furthermore, during the Anglo-German naval talks in London, Britain expressed the hope of reducing the tonnage limit of capital ships from 35,000 tons to 25,000 tons, and the gun caliber from 16 inches to 12 inches. The tonnage limit of cruisers would be reduced from 10,000 tons to 7,000 tons, and the gun caliber from 8 inches to 6 inches. The US Navy Department cannot but pay attention to this British proposal. In the 1930 London Naval Conference, the United States firmly refused to reduce the tonnage limit of each battleship. The reason for the US Navy Department's opposition was that the United States has no naval bases in any of the world's major sea lanes. Therefore, the United States must have capital ships with a displacement of 35,000 tons, armed with 16-inch caliber guns, and cruisers with a displacement of 10,000 tons, armed with 8-inch caliber guns, and with a wide range of activities. This position is in direct contrast to the hopes expressed by Britain in these Anglo-German talks in London. Therefore, the US government is paying close attention to it. Furthermore, the general opinion in the United States is that the United States has played a major role in various naval negotiations after the Great War. However, in this Anglo-German naval negotiation, Britain proceeded without regard for the United States, creating a fait accompli in order to force the United States to recognize it. This makes the general American public feel unhappy. Recalling that before the 1920 London Naval Conference, Prime Minister MacDonald personally came to the United States and concluded an agreement with President Hoover on Anglo-American naval parity, and then returned to Britain to announce the matter. Now, Britain is doing the opposite. Comparing the past with the present, one cannot help but feel a sense of vicissitude. Moreover, the United States believes that this attitude of Britain will inevitably arouse repercussions from France and Italy. The Anglo-German naval agreement has overturned the policy of coordination among Britain, France, and Italy established in Rome, London, Stresa, and Geneva in one fell swoop. As for Britain's optimistic view that this new strategy of Britain will enable European diplomacy to change course and open up new avenues, people in the United States dare not agree with it. (23rd Havas)

(Tokyo) The British government intends to use the Anglo-German naval agreement, which was concluded the day before yesterday, as a starting point for a five-nation disarmament agreement between Britain, the United States, France, Japan, and Italy. Moreover, the content of the Anglo-German agreement adopted the principle of classification-based ratios, which Japan absolutely opposes. Therefore, the attitude of the countries concerned is attracting great attention. The New York Times, Washington Post, and other newspapers oppose the Anglo-German naval agreement as follows: (1) Britain's attempt to use the Anglo-German agreement as a model for a general naval disarmament agreement violates Article 18 of the Treaty of Versailles. (2) Britain's measures are fueling Japan's aggression in China, perhaps because there is no hope of an Anglo-American alliance, but it is inappropriate to submit the fait accompli to the disarmament conference. (24th Telecommunications)

Whether it is the general principles of French foreign policy, or the attitude towards naval or air agreements, France has never changed. Therefore, it has taken special pains to reconcile finance and national defense. Therefore, it requests the necessary funding. If the financial authorities have any hope, they will disclose (1) the reorganization of the financial and tax system, (1) the low-interest refinancing of public bonds, (1) the issuance of public bonds within a certain limit, and (1) the re-negotiation of special accounts. The army, from its own standpoint, has studied methods of saving money and hopes that the financial authorities will handle it properly. (24th Telecommunications)

International Chamber of Commerce Congress: Opened in Paris Yesterday; Trade Issues Discussed First 38

(Paris) The 8th annual meeting of the International Chamber of Commerce Federation opened here this morning, with President Lebrun holding the opening ceremony. The meeting will last for about a week, with more than 1,000 representatives from 48 countries participating. This afternoon, the issue of market competition will be discussed, and Japanese trade competition will also be on the agenda. This discussion will probably attract attention from all parties. In addition, the conference will also discuss stabilizing currencies and tariff issues. (24th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Business representatives from all over the world have arrived today, preparing for the opening ceremony of the International Chamber of Commerce Congress tomorrow. A total of 32 countries are participating in this conference. The plenary meeting tomorrow morning will first discuss the issue of reviving international trade. The chairman will be Dutch representative Van Zeeland. At that time, Van Zeeland will first address the representatives of various countries to welcome them, and then briefly describe the purpose of the meeting. This conference will be held for a week. The mornings will be plenary meetings, with one agenda item discussed each day. On Saturday morning, some financial and economic policies will be decided. The afternoons will be group meetings, discussing various specialized commercial issues. The plenary meeting on Tuesday morning is the most important. At that time, the issue of currency stability will be discussed. The International Chamber of Commerce has been studying this issue for a long time, so at the end of the conference, there will inevitably be a resolution advocating currency stability. As for other issues, Wednesday is the organization of production and distribution, Thursday is the international flow of goods and capital, and Friday is the adjustment of transportation methods. There will also be a special plenary meeting on Friday afternoon to discuss the issue of eliminating obstacles to international trade. (23rd National Telegram)

Bomb Thrown in Front of the US Embassy in Mexico City; Possibly Done by a Patriotic Organization; Only Windows Damaged, No Significant Losses 40

Mexico City: Today, someone threw a bomb into the US Embassy, ​​destroying many windows, but there was no major loss. Local medical authorities cannot fully explain the cause of this incident. Recently, President Cárdenas and former President Calles had differences of opinion, and the whole city felt uneasy. However, the United States and other powers were not involved in this matter. The general public believes that today's bomb was the result of recent rogue marches in the streets. It is still remembered that when US Ambassador Daniels came here two and a half years ago, his relationship with the former president was very close, and patriotic organizations and some newspapers in Mexico opposed him because he was the Secretary of the Navy when the US Navy occupied Mexican territory in 1915. However, after Daniels took office, he was very friendly with the Mexican people. Recently, Daniels praised former President Calles in a speech, which caused displeasure among those who opposed Calles, but there is no evidence to prove that today's bombing was done by that faction. (23rd National Telegram)

Principles and Contents of Income Tax 43

(Nanjing) After considering past cases and the current economic situation, the Ministry of Finance has decided to implement income tax in the 24th year, and has included income tax revenue of 5 million yuan in the revenue part of the national general budget, and has drafted the principles of income tax, which have been submitted to the Central Political Committee for approval. It is only necessary to properly resolve the issue of income donations currently collected by the central government after the income tax is launched, and it can be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. The contents of its income tax principles are as follows: (1) Income tax is a national tax. (2) No surtaxes may be levied on income tax. (3) Income tax will be implemented first for the following two types of income: First, income from profit-making businesses: A. Income from companies, firms, shops, workshops, and factories with capital of more than 3,000 yuan; B. Income from temporary profit-making businesses; Second, income from salaries and remuneration: Income from salaries, public funds, annuities, labor funds, and allowances of civil servants and those engaged in various industries. (4) The scope of those exempt from tax should be listed separately. (5) The method of income tax assessment should adopt a progressive system. (6) The determination of income tax payable should adopt three procedures: declaration, investigation, and review. (7) In the first category, those whose income is less than 5% of their actual capital should be exempt from tax. (8) In the second category, those whose income is less than 500 yuan should be exempt from tax. (24th Central News Agency Telegram)

Plan to Dredge the Wusong River 50

(Nanjing) The Wusong River's water resources are relied upon for irrigation by over seven million mu of farmland in eight counties. It must be dredged every few decades. The Yangtze River Commission has now decided to use mechanized ships for dredging. It has also been agreed with Jiangsu Province and Shanghai Municipality that the section from Xu Gongdun to Panlonggang will be handled by the provincial government, while the lower reaches from Qin Wangdu to Yuji Dun will be entrusted by the Shanghai Municipal Government to the Dredging Bureau for excavation using mechanized ships. The work, divided into six years, is largely completed. However, the section at Yuji Dun is very winding and poses the greatest obstacle to navigation and water flow. In addition to this, straightening is required, which needs substantial funds and will be handled by the central government. The Economic Commission is now carrying out this project of cutting off bends and opening up new river channels. It requires 150 mu of land, and a request has been sent to the relevant department for approval of the land acquisition. (Special dispatch, 24th)

(Tianjin) The Yongding River dredging project is progressing actively. The section from Wengu Port to Yuba Estuary is scheduled to be completed on June 29th, and the rest will also be fully completed soon. (Central News Agency dispatch, 24th)

International Commercial Telegram – Special Reuters Business Report, June 24th – 61

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 140 shillings and 11.5 pence, down 1.5 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market opened very quietly today, but later, large sales from India, and purchases from the United States, China, and speculators when prices fell, made the closing market stable. The spot price was 31.5 pence, and the futures price was 31.75 pence, both down 8.125. The US silver market in Montclair opened about 100 pounds lower, expressing sympathy with the London and Mumbai market conditions.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was very quiet this morning. The exchange rate of British money against the franc and other gold coins generally did not change much. The British-American exchange rate opened at 4.994, the same as the last US-British closing price. There were no fluctuations in the first hour, falling 0.0615 at noon, falling 0.125 at 1:00 pm, but rising 0.125 at 2:00 pm, to 4.939375.

British-French: Opened unchanged, still at 74.62 francs. After the first hour, it rose one pound. The price was 74.60 francs at 2:00 pm, which was two pounds lower than the opening.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market fell slightly today, because cotton-producing states continued to report good weather. Prices later rose slightly. Many operators were pessimistic, fearing that manufacturers would reduce production even more in August than before.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was stable today. At 1:00 pm, the November futures price was 6.04, up one pound from the previous close. British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was sluggish and lacked excitement this morning. Prices changed after hearing of sales in the American wheat market. In the afternoon, the October futures price was 5 shillings and 3.875 pence, 0.375 pence lower than the Saturday close.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened sharply lower due to good news from Liverpool and a larger Canadian wheat harvest, but later prices tended to rebound. Grain prices also fell first and then rose.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet today, but prices were relatively stable. At noon, the trading prices for July and September futures were 6.125 pence, the same as the closing price on the 6th.

New York: The New York rubber market was quiet and stable this morning, showing sympathy with the London market. Prices rose slightly at the opening, but there were no subsequent changes.

Securities

New York: New York securities prices mostly rose slightly at the opening today, and trading was relatively active. Thereafter, there was some variation. Although oil and copper stocks were slightly looser, most of the opening gains could be maintained. Merchants were awaiting definite news about President Roosevelt's new tax proposals. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average was 120.86, up eleven pounds. The prices are as follows:

After Song Zheyuan's Removal, Situation of the Zhangbei Incident, Qin Dechun Will Start Negotiations with Matsui, The Original Troops Stationed in Zhangbei Will Be Transferred Elsewhere 75

Beijing Correspondence, The Hebei issue and Zhangbei Incident, through repeated negotiations, the Hebei issue is generally resolved, the remaining outstanding matters are awaiting the acting chairman of the Political Readjustment Committee, Wang Kemin, to discuss with the Japanese side's Sakai and Doihara in Beijing. Wang arrived in Tianjin this morning (22nd) and met Sakai in the afternoon. Doihara is waiting for Wang in Beijing, and a detailed consultation on the Zhangbei Incident will be held after Wang arrives in Beijing tomorrow. Regarding the Zhangbei Incident, since the chairman of Chahar, Song Zheyuan, has been dismissed, he will immediately come to Beijing and transfer to Tianjin. The chairmanship will be taken over by Qin Dechun. The position of commander of the 29th Army is temporarily entrusted to Zhang Zizhong, commander of the 38th Division, to be responsible. Song himself is recuperating in Tianjin and will not go elsewhere for the time being. The central government is devising other arrangements for the 29th Army's defense area. The 132nd Division troops originally stationed in the Zhangbei area have recently moved south to Wanquan. Once the defense area is determined, they will all be transferred elsewhere. Matsui, the Japanese military liaison officer stationed in Zhangjiakou responsible for negotiating the Zhangbei Incident, arrived in Beijing a few days ago and is waiting to meet with Qin Dechun. Qin arrived in Beijing this morning (22nd) and agreed with Matsui to start negotiations tomorrow (23rd). According to Qin's remarks to reporters, the Zhangbei negotiations are being consulted directly and indirectly by relevant parties and have not yet reached a final resolution. He personally adheres to the greatest sincerity in handling this matter. As for the important aspects of the steps involved, he must report and ask for instructions from the central government. After having some contact with the negotiation matters in Beijing, he will go to Tianjin in a private capacity to visit the former chairman Song Zheyuan for his illness, etc. According to Matsui's remarks, he will meet with Qin Dechun on the Zhangbei Incident and conduct the first step of negotiations. The detailed method, whether to discuss it in Beijing or Zhangjiakou, must be decided after meeting Qin.

The position of Tianjin Mayor was initially announced as Wang Kemin's appointment, but Wang's consent was not obtained beforehand. Wang strongly declined the position. This time, he came north to take the position of acting chairman of the Political Readjustment Committee, with the condition that he would not take the position of Tianjin Mayor. Therefore, the central government temporarily ordered Shang Zhen to serve concurrently. Shang's acting as this position is temporary in nature. The official successor is currently being searched for, but there are quite a few competitors at present. (June 22nd)

Japanese Planes Reconnoiter Baoding for Days, Troops Stationed in Baoding Have Completed Transfer, 4,000 Special Police Arrive in Baoding to Add Defenses 76

Baoding Correspondence, After the Hebei Provincial Government moved to Baoding, Baoding has become the capital of the province. The once silent and desolate Baoding city has gradually revealed a lively scene. All industries such as inns and restaurants have benefited threefold. The population of the entire city has also increased by 5,000 to 6,000 people compared to before. At the beginning of the provincial government's move to Baoding, the 51st Army under the command of Yu Xuezhong followed and moved to Baoding to maintain the security of the provincial capital. Later, Yu's troops were transferred to Shaanxi to suppress bandits. The 2nd Division of Huang Jie, originally stationed in Baoding, was ordered to move to Xuzhou. The defense of Baoding city was empty, and with the repeated reconnaissance of Japanese planes in Baoding in recent days, people were panicked to the extreme. The provincial government plans to transfer 4,000 special police officers from Caicun to Baoding to maintain the security of the provincial capital. The Military Branch will also transfer the 2nd Cavalry Division of the 32nd Army to station in the urban and rural areas of Baoding to assist in defense. The current situation of various parties here and the situation of various armies passing through Baoding and Nankai are described separately below.

Japanese Aircraft Reconnoiter Daily

Since June 15th, Japanese aircraft have been coming to Baoding for reconnaissance several times every day. Their pretext is to investigate whether our army is opening south. Since June 15th, Japanese aircraft must fly from the northeast along the Pinghan Railway at 11:00 am or 10:40 am every day. When they fly over the city of Baoding, they fly around several times, and then fly southwest along the Pinghan Railway. Every time the Japanese aircraft arrive, they must first go to the Nanguan Airport and the 24th Cavalry Brigade's defense area to fly low and inspect. Previously, on the morning of the 17th, at 10:00 am, two Japanese aircraft came to Baoding, and one actually landed at Nanguan Airport. The next day, a person from Nanxiang came to talk, saying that the landed Japanese aircraft carried three Japanese people, all of whom got off the plane and spied near Nanfang Tongren Middle School for a long time before boarding the plane and taking off. In recent days, they have come to Baoding without interruption, causing extreme panic among the people.

Yu's Troops Have All Left

After Yu Xuezhong was transferred to the commander of the bandit suppression area in the three provinces of Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, Yu's 51st Army was ordered to move to Fengxiang, Shaanxi. The three divisions under the jurisdiction of the army, Chen Guanqun, Du Jiwu, and Li Zhentang, have all left Baoding and gone to Zhengzhou one after another, and then entered Shaanxi. The eight departments of the military headquarters also left Baoding for Shaanxi on the 17th, led by Chief of Staff Liu Zhonggan. Currently, the vanguard troops and military personnel have arrived in Fengxiang, Shaanxi, to arrange everything. The personnel remaining in Baoding will also go to Shaanxi on the 20th. Baoding has no remnants of the 51st Army. Yu Xuezhong himself is now going to Sichuan to meet Chiang and, after meeting Chiang and asking for instructions, will go directly to Fengxiang to organize the Bandit Suppression Command.

17th Army Headquarters Moved to Nanjing

The headquarters of the 17th Army, originally stationed in Baoding Guangyuan, was originally planned to be transferred to Beiping when the provincial government moved to Baoding, but it was not realized. Therefore, the Military Commission changed the deployment of the army headquarters to Nanjing. Currently, the personnel of the army and the guard battalion have completely left Baoding for the south on the 20th, and passed through Zhengzhou to Nanjing. As for the Guangyuan houses, they will be vacated for the Finance Department to occupy. Currently, the 17th Army Headquarters has all been moved out, and the Finance Department should have moved into Guangyuan to work.

The First Division of the Army Moved to Xuzhou

The 2nd Division of the Army, commanded by Huang Jie, was originally stationed in the suburbs of Baoding, and the division headquarters was located in the palace. The division has now been ordered to move to Xuzhou. The 4th Brigade, the 6th Brigade, and the 24th Cavalry Brigade under its command have successively passed through Baoding. Huang Jie himself and the division headquarters also went south on the 21st, passing through Zhengzhou to Xuzhou. More than 60 representatives of various agencies in Baoding specially held a public banquet for Huang at Lianhua Pond the other day. During the banquet, Huang gave a passionate speech, and all the participants were in tears. Huang's family also went south with him the other day.

The Public Security Bureau Is Being Reorganized

After the provincial government moved to Baoding, the Baoding Special Public Security Bureau was originally scheduled to be reorganized into the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. At the 626th regular meeting of the provincial government, Zhang Houwan, the acting chairman, specifically proposed the reorganization of the Public Security Bureau, which was passed as proposed and issued a notice on the 21st, stating that the Baoding Special Public Security Bureau should be reorganized into the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. Miao Zuoxin was commissioned to act as the director. On the same day, the provincial government also instructed the bureau to immediately abolish the Special Public Security Bureau and change it to the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. After receiving the order, the bureau complied with the order and began reorganization. Although the internal structure has been slightly expanded, it is still being streamlined. Due to the limited funding, the number of police officers has been temporarily decided not to increase. Furthermore, in view of the fact that the provincial government has come to Baoding, the bureau is planning a comprehensive prevention plan for the security of Baoding. All police positions and traffic arteries, as well as city gates and stations, have been ordered to be properly maintained.

Special Police Arrive in Baoding to Add Defenses

After the departure of the 51st Army, the 17th Army, and the 2nd Division, the defense of Baoding was deeply felt to be empty. Although there are a small number of police and security teams from the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau to maintain security, their strength is still weak. Moreover, the security of the four suburbs is particularly important. Therefore, the provincial government decided to transfer 4,000 special police officers trained previously from Caicun to add defenses. It is said that there are a total of 9,000 special police officers, and 5,000 have already entered the so-called war zone, while the remaining 4,000 are still in Caicun. Furthermore, the 2nd Cavalry Division of the 32nd Army will also be moved to the four suburbs of Baoding. Currently, the deputy officer of the division has been sent to Baoding to survey the defense area. They will be able to come soon. (June 22nd)

Haiqi and Hai琛 Ships: Escape from Guangdong Waters, Anchoring in Hong Kong for Coal and Food Resupply; Jiang Xiyuan Detained in Guangzhou 77

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Haiqi and Hai琛 ships, since secretly escaping from Huangpu on the evening of the 15th, were discovered by the Huangpu garrison's salt police and special task force, who used door guns to stop them. At the same time, the fish farm and Changzhou forts opened fire and bombarded them. The Haiqi ships also fired back, fighting and retreating, until they ran aground near Lianhua Mountain at the exit of the East River. At this time, the provincial military authorities, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched airplanes to pursue them. The two ships then used delaying tactics, sending three representatives to the province on the evening of the 16th, requesting repentance and begging Guangdong to re-accept them and not pursue past offenses. Chen Jitang expressed his opinion, saying that if the two ships were willing to stay, other solutions could be discussed, otherwise, their departure was not a pity. As for the negotiation and mediation methods, the headquarters drafted three responses, roughly: 1. The Haiqi and Hai琛 ships must sail back to Huangpu; 2. All officers and soldiers of the two ships must disembark in Huangpu to listen to instructions; 3. The issue of salary payments will be considered again. However, while the representatives were replying, there was a sudden downpour, and the two ships believed that the time had come. Taking advantage of the heavy rain and darkness, the airplanes could not take off to pursue them, and the tide was high at this time, so they immediately fired up their engines and sailed past Humen. At that time, the Humen forts opened fire to intercept them, and the Haiqi and Hai琛 ships also fired back, defending themselves. After an hour of fierce battle, the searchlight of the Humen fort was destroyed by artillery fire, reducing the target for the two ships, and they were able to break through Humen, sailing along Jinxingmen and Tangjiawan in Zhongshan, across Lingdingyang, and toward Chiwan in Hong Kong's territorial waters. When the two ships left, they had already sent a telegram to Hong Kong, saying that there were wounded soldiers who would land in Hong Kong and be sent to the hospital for treatment. On the 17th, around 6:00 AM, the two ships anchored in the waters of Chiwan, engaged in internal repairs. Then, four wounded soldiers from the Haiqi ship were sent to Hong Kong by boat and admitted to the National Hospital for treatment. After the Haiqi ship anchored in Chiwan, it sent personnel to Hong Kong for several days to purchase coal and food, preparing to set sail for other destinations at any time. It is said that when the two ships launched the mutiny, the captain of the Haiqi ship, Chen Hao, was tied up by the officers and soldiers. The captain of the Hai琛 ship, Fang Nianzu, was fortunately not on board. When the mutiny was launched, it was commanded by a Tang, the former captain of the Fu You ship. The hull of the Haiqi ship was damaged by airplane bombs and fort artillery fire, reaching almost four-tenths of the entire ship. After the two ships arrived in Hong Kong waters, Guangdong lifted martial law, and ship traffic between Guangdong and Hong Kong was restored. The garrison near Huangpu was also withdrawn. Li Jiezhi, the commander of the Humen Fortress, came to the province on the 18th to report the interception of the two ships. Zhang Zhiying, the vice commander of the Navy, accompanied by the chief of staff, took a ship to Huangpu on the 18th to inspect the area and summon students from the naval academy for instruction. Furthermore, the naval vice commander, Jiang Xiyuan (Yan Zhong), was not involved in the vortex this time, although he had no responsibility to bear. However, the authorities believed that the Bohai Fleet was led by Jiang to the south, and this time, the Haiqi and Hai琛 ships mutinied, not without suspicion, so Jiang was detained for investigation. (June 19th)

Wuhan Suffers Several Days of Heavy Rain, the Yangtze River Rises Sharply; Collapse of Houses in Heavy Rain, a Tragic Event with Nearly 100 Deaths and Injuries; Zhang Qun Postpones Departure for Dike Inspection Due to Official Trip to Beijing 78

Hankou Correspondence: Since the beginning of summer, the climate in Wuhan has been extremely hot, and the Fahrenheit thermometer has reached 100 degrees. The citizens were hoping for rain very eagerly. On the 19th of this month, heavy rain suddenly fell, lasting for several days, and the temperature dropped to 70 degrees. It was still cold even with lined clothing, just like late spring or mid-autumn. The water level of the Yangtze River increased daily. On the 22nd, the rain was even heavier, and it did not stop until the next morning. Coupled with thunder and lightning, it continued all night. Low-lying streets and markets were all turned into swamps, and transportation was blocked as a result. The homes of poor people outside the Pinghan Railway were especially flooded, and the poor people were living in the water, suffering greatly. At dawn on the 23rd, the city government began to build temporary sheds along Zhongzheng Road to accommodate them as much as possible. During the heavy rain, the houses at Nos. 342, 344, and 346 of Maishantang Street outside Zhongshan Road suddenly collapsed. Because it was late at night, and the event was sudden, hundreds of residents were either killed or injured, with no one spared. Also, in the prosperous area of Houshengli at the entrance of Zhongshan Road, the water was two feet deep, drowning a Ding姓 child, which was also tragic. As for the water level of the Yangtze River, it rose sharply by 1.2 meters on the 23rd, and the Jianghan Customs water mark reached 35.7 feet, not far from the shore. The Wuhan Flood Prevention Association, considering the situation to be very serious, began working day and night from now on to avoid danger. Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun originally planned to depart with Yang Silian, director of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau, to inspect the dikes in various counties, but he was temporarily summoned by President Wang on the evening of the 22nd to take the Jianghua liner to Beijing to discuss important matters and could not go. Yang is scheduled to depart on the 24th. (23rd)

Qiantang River Water Level Rises Suddenly, Sea Dike Silt Washed Away Dozens of Feet; Zhuji Dongbi Lake Dike Collapses; Hangzhou-Huizhou and Hangzhou-Fuyang Highways are Blocked 79

Hangzhou Correspondence: Continuous heavy rain has caused the water level of the Qiantang River to rise sharply. Furthermore, mountain water from the upper reaches flowed downstream, causing the Qiantang River water level at the Zhakou to suddenly rise to 8.1 meters, an increase of more than 2 meters compared to before. On the 23rd, the water continued to recede, and the water level continued to rise to 8.6 meters. The Nanfeng and Xixing wharves were once submerged by water. The situation was quite critical. The Hangzhou Municipal Government and the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau dispatched personnel to inspect the sea dikes. If there were any accidents, they would immediately send workers to rescue them. Fortunately, the situation eased slightly in the evening, and the water level dropped by 2.3 centimeters. Today (24th), the rain has stopped and the sky has cleared. According to the report from the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, the highest water level has dropped to 7.5 meters. If a large amount of mountain water from the upper reaches does not continue to attack, the sea dike should not be in danger. Furthermore, the Department of Construction, according to a telegram from the Hangzhou Sea Dike Engineering Office, reported that the silt outside the dike in the area from Babu to Tasan in Haining was eroded by huge waves, and dozens of feet had collapsed. The newly built submerged dam was also destroyed, and the dike body was in a dangerous state. It immediately sent the responsible section staff Jiang Min to investigate and strictly supervise prevention and rescue, and protect the dike body. Also, the province received an urgent telegram from Zhuji County reporting that the Dongbi Lake dike was destroyed by floods and was completely submerged. Work could no longer proceed, and 500 workers had stopped working. County Magistrate Li Yuguang happened to be in the province on official business and had discussed prevention and rescue measures with the Water Conservancy Bureau. Furthermore, on the Hangzhou-Huizhou Highway, about 20 kilometers from the Zhejiang border Yuling Pass at Zhongling, mountain soil on the ridge was washed away by heavy rain on the 23rd. With a crash, it poured onto the road below the mountain, crushing more than a dozen civilian houses along the road, and six or seven farmers were crushed to death because they could not escape in time. The Hangzhou-Huizhou direct passenger car only ran to Yuling Pass due to road damage. The Yushu Company has dispatched workers to rush repairs, and traffic is expected to resume in about two days. Furthermore, the water on the Hangzhou-Fuyang Highway rose by two feet in the Gaotai and Fuyang sections due to the large increase in mountain water that could not be discharged, and traffic was blocked. The water level gradually receded this afternoon, and traffic can resume normally tomorrow (25th). According to Mao Yisheng, director of the Qiantang River Bridge Engineering Office, the large increase in the Qiantang River water level, although inevitably slightly hindered the bridge project, but did not have much impact. (24th)

Songjiang: Rice Merchant Mysteriously Disappears from Zhanggang 80

Cao Lingfeng, a businessman who runs a rice business in Zhangjiagang, more than one li south of Shihudang, has been relatively successful in recent years. However, he has been affected by the economic downturn and has little savings. He suddenly disappeared yesterday morning, which is quite strange. According to reports, neighbors had not seen the Cao family open their door around 9:00 AM yesterday morning, and they were suspicious. They tried to enter the house and found it empty. It was unclear where they had suddenly gone. They then saw writing on the wall, roughly saying that they would reply within a few days. Whether they were kidnapped or murdered is being discussed, and a strict investigation is needed to confirm.

True Cholera Discovered in the City 81

Recently, there have been two cases in this city of true cholera that were treated and died. One was A Jun, a tea worker from the tax collection office, who suddenly felt severe abdominal pain and diarrhea a few days ago. He was sent to Ruose Hospital for diagnosis and treatment that night, but eventually died yesterday. The other was A Shi, the daughter of a comb maker on Fozibqiao, who also had severe abdominal pain, vomiting, and diarrhea a few days ago. The diagnosis was true cholera, and she died soon after. Some say that the unclean water is an important cause.

Wuxi: Financial Sector Tightens Lending 82

During the heyday of silk factories in the 18th year of the Republic of China, there were more than 20 remittance banks in this city. Later, as the silk market declined and silk factories closed down, the remittance banks suffered heavy losses as a result and could not maintain operations, and they closed down one after another. Only Chenghengfeng, Fuyuan, Shenyu, Yuanfengsheng, Ruichang, Fuyu, De, Changsheng, and Zengda and other nine are left. There are 11 banks, including China, Communications, Jiangsu, Farmers, Shanghai, Mainland, Central South, Industry, Communications, Industry, and Xinhua. Because of their strong capital and stable lending, their business is booming, and they have a surplus. Banks mostly pay attention to collateral when lending, and there is very little credit lending, so the failure of silk factories did not have much impact on banks. When spring cocoons were put on the market this year, only more than 1.5 million loans were issued. This time, wheat is being put on the market, and the rice industry urgently needs loans, but the financial sector has tightened lending to the extreme, and the situation is quite deserted, less than one-third of what it was in previous years. Furthermore, there are 32 silk factories in the entire county, with 9,490 silk looms. Some of them are still operating on behalf of others. In addition, industries such as silk fabrics and Nanhua can only maintain expenses. Social finance is becoming increasingly difficult, and it is difficult to be optimistic about the future of business.

Drug Pellet Criminal Sentenced to Life Imprisonment 83

On September 5th last year, the County Public Security Bureau arrested eight drug pellet criminals, including Chen Shaokun, in Nanyangli No. 10 and Silangjun Lane No. 1 inside Guangfumen, and seized 109,000 drug pellets. They were presented to the county government and then to the Zhenjiang Garrison Headquarters. Chen Shaokun has now been sentenced to life imprisonment, Wang Hushi to 15 years imprisonment, Hu Qiushi and Yang Axue to 13 years each, Chen Yangshi to 12 years, and Yang Shishi, Chen Zhushi, and Wu Yike were acquitted. They were sent back to the Wuxi County Government yesterday for separate execution.

All agencies currently residing in the school must move out before July 15th.

Haimen Robbers Search and Kill the Victim 85

At about 9:00 PM on the 22nd, seven or eight robbers suddenly came to the home of Ma Tingzhen, a villager in Guguxiang, Qidong District. They broke into the house, tied up Ma, and forbade him from making a sound. Then, they turned over boxes and cabinets and searched at will. They left after a long time. Then, they went to the homes of neighbors Tang Yongkang and Wu Chaosheng to search. Wu resisted with weapons and was shot in the abdomen by the robbers and fell to the ground and died. At the time, the villagers heard the alarm and gathered to surround and arrest them. Seeing that the situation was not good, the robbers took the stolen goods and fled. After inventory, Ma Tingzhen's family lost five yuan in banknotes, five bolts of white cloth, and three cloth tents. Tang Shuikang's family lost five bolts of white cloth, and Wu Chaosheng's family lost more than ten pieces of clothing. On the 23rd, the victim reported to the county government, and Chai Cheng arrived to inspect the scene. Wu Chaosheng was indeed shot and killed by robbers. The family was ordered to collect the body and await the arrest and investigation of the murderer.

Nanjing President Wang Promotes Frugal Weddings 86

The current secretary of the Executive Yuan, Zhu Qi, is President Wang's nephew. He graduated from the University of Paris in France. Recently, through the introduction of Mr. Chu Minyi and Chen Yunwen, he was engaged to Ms. He, a fellow villager. On the 22nd, a wedding ceremony was held at the Nanjing Overseas Chinese Hostel. Mr. Chen Shuren was the wedding officiant. President Wang, feeling the economic downturn, market depression, and difficult resources in society, advocated frugality and abolished all the complicated formalities of old-fashioned marriages. He did not send out wedding invitations widely in advance, so few people outside the family knew about it except for a few relatives and friends. On the day, only Zeng Zhongming, Xu Mo, and dozens of relatives and friends attended. After the wedding ceremony, everyone was treated with tea and snacks, each of which was only worth five cents. The total cost was about 100 yuan. Such a simple and frugal wedding, done by a party-state leader, is even more commendable. When people across the country hold weddings, if there is no place to gather and hold weddings, they can all be used as models.

Xiaoshan: 30,000 Mu of Sand Land Collapses in Xiaosibu 90

Xiaosibu, Toutong Township, Dongxiang, Xiaoshan, is located on the opposite bank of Haining County and is densely populated. There were originally about 30,000 mu of sand land along the river, but in recent years, the river has changed drastically, and the tides are unprecedentedly high. Therefore, the river has collapsed in less than a year, and 10,000 mu of mature sand land have been lost to the ocean. Many residents have moved away. Recently, the river collapse there has been serious, and the situation is extremely dangerous. For example, the Gao Zhengxing Public Office base and Shaodui street base there have already fallen into the water, and the street houses are being demolished one after another, and some are even unable to move. The poor and helpless people are suffering the disaster of river collapse, displaced and filled with wailing, which is unbearable to witness. It is hoped that the authorities will find ways to provide relief.

Local News

Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Conference Closed Yesterday; Minister Kong and Director Wu Attended and Gave Instructions 91

The conference of directors of the stamp, tobacco, and alcohol tax bureaus of the Tax Administration closed yesterday morning. The closing ceremony was originally scheduled to be held in the Joonpoo Bureau conference room on the fifth floor of the Jianghai Customs. Around ten o'clock, the directors of various provincial bureaus, Zhao Xien, Sheng Shengyuan, Ding Chungao, etc., and the director of the Tax Administration, Wu Qiding, as well as 29 people from the secretary section of the administration, arrived at the meeting one after another. The order of the closing ceremony was: 1. All stood at attention; 2. Paid the highest respect to the party-state flag and the portrait of the Premier; 3. The chairman respectfully read the Premier's will; 4. Silence; 5. The Minister of Finance delivered a speech; 6. The Director delivered a speech; 7. The directors of various provincial bureaus gave replies. Then, Director Wu went to the Central Bank to ask Minister Kong for instructions, who instructed him to change the venue to the conference hall on the third floor of the Central Bank. Director Wu then invited everyone to go there. The ceremony began at half past eleven and ended around one o'clock. The instructions of Minister Kong and Director Wu, and the replies of the directors of the provincial bureaus are recorded below.

Minister's Instructions

Minister Kong said in his instructions: Today is the closing day of the conference. You will soon be returning to your posts. I would like to take this opportunity to offer a few words of farewell, and I hope you will be mindful of the difficulties of the times and pay close attention to them. You have been appointed by the government to manage the salt administration of the provincial bureaus, and your responsibilities are extremely important. You must know that in our service, the first thing is to be worthy of the country, and the second is to be worthy of our conscience. Now that the country is in great difficulty, we must do our best to rectify things to increase tax revenue. You must know that as provincial bureau directors, not only must you be honest and restrained yourselves, but you must also be responsible for the people you employ. If the people you employ make even a small mistake, it is your own fault. I have repeatedly received letters and telegrams from Chairman Chiang, who often mentions the corruption in tax collection agencies in various places. During this suppression period, most provinces are under the jurisdiction of the Headquarters, and if corruption is found, it can be dealt with at any time according to the law. Do not let the corruption of your subordinates implicate yourselves, so you must take self-cleanliness as the first priority. The stamp, tobacco, and alcohol taxes, the stamp tax has now been changed to be sold by the post office, and the long-standing malpractices have been eliminated. The bureaus only need to earnestly extract funds, and the sales volume will naturally increase day by day. As for tobacco and alcohol, they are consumer goods, and the tax rates in various countries are very high, and they are easy to manage because they are manufactured in factories. China's industry is underdeveloped, and the production of tobacco and alcohol has always been very scattered, especially in the south, which is prone to abuses in collection. In the face of this situation, how should we rectify the tax system? The country is vast, and the situation in each province is different, and even within a province, the situation in different places may be different. How to rectify, how to increase tax revenue, how to promote benefits, and how to eliminate abuses, you must adapt to local conditions, make plans in advance, and put yourselves aside in advance, and act as a third party, so that it is easier to achieve results. The country sets up officials to hold office, and the emphasis is on public affairs. We should serve with the country as the premise, and not treat it as our personal property. As long as we are in office for one day, we should fulfill our responsibilities for one day. All ideas for promoting benefits and eliminating abuses should be contributed as much as possible. Selfishness and self-interest should be thoroughly eliminated, and even requests and favors should be completely eliminated. In the past, officials mostly protected each other, so politics did not get on track. Now we are in an extraordinary period, and we must all cheer up and work hard to save the country, so that the country has a solution. Finance is the mother of all administrations, and no construction can be carried out without money. Tax administration, whether large or small, should pay attention to benefiting the country and facilitating commerce. Mount Tai does not choose soil, and the rivers and seas do not choose small streams, but are formed by accumulation. At present, various provinces often ask for increased funding because of their vast land area and insufficient budget, but they do not know that nothing is immutable. If they can adapt to the times and allocate funds properly, it is not impossible to find a solution. This conference was able to cooperate fully, and I hope that after you return to your bureaus, you will proceed according to the resolutions and your experience, so that both national taxes and commercial sentiment will benefit. This is what I hope for.

Director's Speech

Director of the Tax Administration Wu Qiding then delivered a closing speech, saying: During this conference, you have traveled long distances without fear of fatigue, and your loyalty and sincerity are deeply admired. The long-standing malpractices of the tobacco and alcohol taxes and the difficulties of the business operations of merchants and people are the foundation for urgent rectification. In the opening speech, I briefly described the outline, and I was honored to have the Minister personally give instructions, which were earnest, detailed, and clear. Hearing this made me feel fearful and inspired me to redouble my efforts. I believe that you all share the same feeling. This conference received more than 20 proposals, which were all realistic and pragmatic, and did not focus on empty talk and lofty theories. The participating provinces, from Heng and Xiang in the south to Yan and Ji in the north, and from Min and Jiangxi in the east to Ezhou in the west, gathered together, calmly discussed, and formulated regulations, completing the work quickly. The actual difficulties of various provinces have been conveyed to the central government, and the thorny deployments have been announced to various provinces, and the advantages and disadvantages of tax affairs between provinces have been explained to each other, communicating feelings, eliminating borders, and showing sincerity to each other, so as to obtain cooperation. I am deeply grateful for your ability to cooperate fully. Once the resolutions are submitted to the Ministry for approval, they can be implemented separately. Politics values action, and matters value practice. Our country has always advocated formalism, and there are often errors in valuing reality and following the name. The matters resolved this time are all plans made by you based on your knowledge and experience. Once approved, it is hoped that they will be earnestly implemented and fully realized, and not just entrusted to empty words. The Ministry uses it to task the Administration, the Administration uses it to task the provincial bureaus, and the provincial bureaus use it to task the branch bureaus, with layers of restrictions, aiming for a goal, rewarding the successful and punishing the unsuccessful, and dismissing the dishonest. Everything should be based on the law, without any pretense, so that sitting and talking can lead to action, and results can be seen quickly, both to live up to the Minister's earnest expectations and to save the merchants and people from their plight. Therefore, I always encourage myself, and I also hope that you gentlemen will be able to work together and achieve success together.

Directors' Replies

Zhao Xien, the director of the Zhejiang Bureau, and Sheng Shengyuan, the director of the Jiangsu Bureau, successively gave replies, the general meaning of which was that this conference had been greatly assisted by the Minister twice. After returning to their posts, they would earnestly implement the resolutions of the conference, taking personality as the primary support, aiming at benefiting the country and facilitating commerce, not avoiding difficulties, not resigning from complaints, and working hard to make the country's finances benefit. However, the directors have limited talent and knowledge, and I hope that you will guide and encourage us at any time, which is what we hope for.

Industry and Commerce Loan Committee Holds Third Meeting Yesterday; Approves Loan Outline and Other Regulations; Submits to Ministry of Finance for Approval and Implementation 92

Central News Agency reports: The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Committee has drafted loan outlines and detailed loan rules, etc. After Chairman Cai Zengji paid a visit to Minister of Finance Kong to request approval, the committee convened its third meeting at the Guohuo Bank yesterday afternoon to review and approve them. They will be submitted to the Ministry for approval and implementation. Details are as follows:

Attending Committee Members

The third meeting of the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Committee was held at 4:00 PM yesterday in the meeting room on the second floor of the Guohuo Bank on Henan Road. The committee members present were Cai Zengji, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaosu, Xi Demao, Bei Songsun, Song Ziliang, Wang Yansong, Qin Runqing, Yu Zuoting, Zhang Peishen, and others, totaling eleven people. Wu Xingya was absent due to business, and Wang Yansong represented him.

Matters Decided

After the meeting commenced, Chairman Cai Zengji led the proceedings with due ceremony. The meeting agenda was as follows: (A) Reading of the previous resolutions; (B) Reports: (1) Chairman's report, (2) Committee members' reports; (C) Discussion items: (1) Draft plan for handling guaranteed loans; (2) Review of the draft charter of this committee; (3) Review of the draft procedural rules of this committee; (4) Review of the draft detailed rules for Shanghai industry and commerce guaranteed loans. All the above draft charters and detailed rules were approved after discussion. The Chairman will prepare a document to submit to the Ministry of Finance for approval and promulgation. The meeting adjourned at around 6:00 PM.

Organizational Charter

Yesterday, the organizational charter of the committee was announced as follows: Article 1: The Ministry of Finance, in order to aid the industry and commerce of Shanghai, has specially allocated national treasury bills worth 20 million yuan as a second guarantee for loans. A committee is organized to oversee and review loan matters in accordance with the ten principles for granting loans promulgated by the Ministry of Finance. It is named the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Committee (hereinafter referred to as "this committee"). Article 2: The number of members of this committee is not fixed and shall be appointed by the Minister of Finance. Article 3: The national treasury bills allocated by the Ministry of Finance shall be the responsibility of this committee for safekeeping, but the procedures for receipt and deposit of the bills shall be entrusted to the China Guohuo Bank for handling. Article 4: This committee shall establish a standing committee, and the members shall elect a chairman from among themselves. Article 5: This committee shall have one executive officer, who shall be nominated by the chairman and appointed with the approval of the committee meeting and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. Article 6: This committee may, depending on the complexity of the matters, establish several specialists, clerks, and secretaries, who shall be appointed by the chairman. Article 7: Matters resolved by this committee shall be implemented by the chairman. Article 8: The standing committee represents this committee and is responsible for supervising and coordinating the implementation of resolutions. Article 9: The executive officer of this committee shall handle the daily affairs of this committee in accordance with the instructions of the chairman and the standing committee. Article 10: Meetings of this committee and the standing committee shall be convened by the chairman. Article 11: When the chairman of this committee is unable to attend a meeting due to business, the standing committee shall convene the meeting. Each member must attend the meeting in person. If a member is unable to attend due to an accident, he may entrust another member of the committee to attend on his behalf, but must declare it in writing in advance. Each member representing another member is limited to representing only one person. Article 13: Matters handled by this committee, except for those with serious circumstances that require special reporting to the Ministry of Finance for review at any time, routine cases shall be reported monthly for record. Article 14: The members of this committee are non-salaried positions. Article 15: The expenses of this committee shall be approved and allocated by the Ministry of Finance. Article 16: The operating procedures, meeting rules, and detailed loan rules of this committee shall be determined separately. Article 17: This committee is temporarily located within the Guohuo Bank. Article 18: Matters not covered in this charter may be resolved by this committee and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and amendment. Article 19: This charter shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Ministry of Finance.

Other Regulations

It is also reported that the guaranteed loan outline, which was approved at the same time, was formulated based on the ten-point outline for aiding industry and commerce previously promulgated by the Ministry of Finance. The original text contains seventeen articles. The detailed loan rules stipulate the procedures for requesting assistance and reviewing loan applications. The operating rules stipulate the responsibilities of each group within the committee. All three items will be submitted to the Ministry for approval and promulgation.

Visit to Kong to Report

New Voice News Agency reports: Gu Yigu, General Manager of the Bank of Communications; Song Ziliang, General Manager of the China Guohuo Bank; Xi Demao, Manager of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank; Bei Songsun, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China; and Zhang Peishen, Manager of the Business Bureau of the Bank of Communications, visited Xu Kan, Vice Minister of Finance, at the Central Bank yesterday morning, starting at 10:30 AM, to discuss matters related to the Money Industry Supervision Committee and the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Committee. Gu left at 11:00 AM, while Xi, Bei, and Zhang left after 11:00 AM. Song left at around 12:00 PM. At 6:30 PM in the afternoon, Chen Guangfu and Song Ziliang, standing committee members of the Industry and Commerce Loan Committee, visited Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi at the Central Bank and left at 6:50 PM. It is reported that they were reporting on the resolutions of the committee meeting.

Loans at the Beginning of the Month

A reporter from the New Voice News Agency learned from the committee yesterday that the office of the committee, located in the building of the China Guohuo Bank, has been prepared. After the organizational charter and loan outline are approved by the Ministry of Finance, it will officially commence operations. The outline stipulates that everything will be handled in accordance with the ten principles promulgated by the Ministry, to assist factories manufacturing domestic goods, merchants selling domestic goods, specialized personnel transporting domestic goods, and undertaking investigation and guidance work. The loan period shall not exceed one year. Those who pass the review by the committee may apply for loans from the banks or money shops designated by the committee. As for the implementation date, it is expected to be in early July.

Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau Expands Simple Life Insurance; Adds Three More Units Besides the Original One; Plans to Hold Service Personnel Training in Shanghai Regularly 95

The Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation is actively preparing to establish simple life insurance services in Beijing, Shanghai, and Hankou. The insurance division within the Bureau is also expanding its scope, adding three units, and plans to conduct training for working service personnel on a regular basis. Once the simple life insurance regulations are approved, it will officially commence operations. The details are as follows, as reported by a reporter from the Ta Kung Pao:

Joint Efforts in Three Locations

The state-run simple life insurance was ordered by the Ministry of Transportation to the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau to first establish branches in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou, and then promote it throughout the country. In Shanghai, in addition to the Bureau and the Shanghai Postal Administration jointly preparing in the branch offices in various important areas such as Nanshi, Zhabei, the French Concession, and the International Settlement, it also ordered the Nanjing Savings and Remittances Branch and the Jiangsu District Postal Administration, the Hankou Savings and Remittances Branch and the Hubei District Postal Administration to jointly prepare. A simple life insurance department will be established first in each branch office, and the sub-branches below the branch office will be temporarily suspended.

Expanding Internal Scope

The insurance division of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau originally had only one unit, handling various general insurance and mail insurance matters. Now, due to the addition of simple life insurance, the workload has increased, so three more units have been added. It is stipulated that the first, second, and third units will specialize in handling simple life insurance matters, as well as general insurance. The fourth unit will be responsible for insurance for mail and packages. Each unit was established within the past week, and the number of staff has also been increased accordingly.

Training Service Personnel

The simple life insurance business is a new venture in China, entirely state-run, and different in nature from the insurance offered by ordinary foreign companies. The procedures and internal organization are very complex. In order to train personnel to handle this business, the Savings and Remittances Bureau has stipulated that each branch office in Beijing, Shanghai, and Hankou will select one or two current postal and savings and remittances staff members for short-term training. The location is set at the Shanghai Bureau. Preparations for the opening of the class have already begun. After this group of service personnel is trained, they will indirectly train the staff of the sub-branches.

Implementation Delayed Beyond July 1st

Regarding the official start date of simple life insurance, the Ministry of Transportation originally planned to implement it from July 1st. Yesterday, according to Zhang Mingxin, Deputy Director of the Insurance Department, the Simple Life Insurance Law was passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government. After the Bureau drafted 75 articles of regulations and submitted them to the Ministry of Transportation for instructions, the Ministry forwarded them to the Executive Yuan in accordance with legal procedures. So far, they have not been approved. At the same time, the preparatory procedures in various places are complicated and time-consuming, so it is estimated that it will not be implemented until early August.

Yao Huanzhou Returns to Shanghai Yesterday After Inspecting the Fisheries of Qingdao and Dalian 98

The Ministry of Industry, considering that the fish market built by the ministry in Shanghai is scheduled to be completed next month, specially dispatched Yao Huanzhou, a member of the fish market preparation committee, to Qingdao and Dalian to inspect the various conditions of the fish markets in various places in order to have reference materials. After receiving the order, Yao left Shanghai on the 4th of this month and visited Qingdao, Yantai, Dalian, and other places. He has now completed the inspection and returned to Shanghai yesterday by the Dalian Maru. The fish market in Dalian is entirely run by the Japanese, with an annual turnover of 4 million yuan. The fish market in Shanghai will be completed next month and will start operations at the end of August. It is estimated that the annual turnover will reach 20 million yuan.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: The Jiahe Wheel Did Not Collide with the Buoy 99

The Jiahe wheel of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company entered from Xiamen on the 20th of this month and was reported to have hit the Taikoo buoy at the Xin Kai River. It was reported in the previous newspaper. It is now learned that after the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received a letter from Taikoo requesting compensation, the company inquired with the captain and crew of the Jiahe wheel, who all stated that there was no collision with the buoy. Moreover, after on-site inspection, although the lower end of the buoy was damaged, there were no scratch marks on the paint on the upper end. If the degree of damage to the lower section of the buoy is observed, the blades of the Jiahe wheel would inevitably be damaged. Now, after sending someone into the water to inspect, the Jiahe wheel blades are not damaged at all, which clearly shows that it was not the Jiahe wheel that collided. The company firmly denies the accusation based on the facts.

Furthermore, it was previously reported in this newspaper that after the Jiahe wheel collided with the buoy, the insurance company was notified to send personnel to inspect and repair it. According to the regulations, collisions of ships with docks and buoys are not within the scope of insurance compensation, so the insurance company is not responsible.
