Social Affairs Bureau Actively Prepares for Cooperative Movement Promotion in This City; The First Preparatory Committee Meeting Yesterday Approved the Outline of the Plan; Opening Ceremony on October 1st in the City Government Auditorium 102

Ta Kung Pao reports: October 1st is the International Day of Cooperatives. The Central Government has stipulated that this day to the 7th is Cooperative Promotion Week. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau plans to hold expanded promotions in conjunction with various agencies and organizations, actively promoting cooperative undertakings, because this year is the year of social construction in this city. The bureau also convened the first preparatory meeting at the China Economic Credit Cooperative on Edward Road yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM and approved the outline of the promotion plan. The details are as follows:

First Preparatory Meeting

The preparatory meeting for Cooperative Promotion Week in this city was held at the China Economic Credit Cooperative on Edward Road yesterday afternoon. The attendees included Zhang Binghui, Wu Xiangru, Shi Gang of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Long Yuting of the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Huang Zao of the Municipal Education Association, etc. Zhang Donghui presided over the meeting. The chairman first reported the purpose of the organization, and then the following resolutions were passed: (1) Approved the outline of the expanded promotion plan for Shanghai Cooperative Promotion Week; (2) Preparing to divide into general affairs and propaganda groups to carry out the work; (3) The next preparatory meeting is scheduled for this Friday (the 18th) at the same location. The meeting adjourned. The outline of the promotion plan is recorded on the right.

Opening Ceremony on July 1st

The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held at the City Government Auditorium on July 1st. This day was originally a joint memorial week for the various bureaus. It is proposed to hold the opening ceremony of the cooperative promotion week at the same time. In addition to the colleagues from the various bureaus participating as a group, letters are sent to various factories, trade unions, municipal councilors, schools at all levels, etc., and a letter is sent to the party headquarters to send representatives to participate in the ceremony. The mayor, bureau chiefs, and experts are invited to speak, and the daily newspapers publish a special issue. The bureau liaises with the various newspapers in advance for this publication, which is edited by each newspaper, and the bureau provides the materials. Airplanes fly around the city and distribute leaflets.

Widespread Promotion

The second day is widespread promotion. The bureau and the education bureau contact the major radio stations in the city separately and allocate a considerable amount of time during the day and night for broadcasting. The preparatory committee invites specialists to broadcast cooperative lectures every night. During the day, the bureau and the education bureau are responsible for giving lectures separately and specifically contact the entertainment industry to broadcast special programs.

District Promotion

The third day is district promotion. The promotion on this day is held in four locations. The South Shanghai district is designated as the People's Education Center on Wenmiao Road, Zhabei is designated as Jianguo Middle School, and Pudong and Wusong are selected by the municipal councilors and farmers' associations in each district, in conjunction with the party headquarters, at appropriate locations, and lectures on cooperative promotion are held. The preparatory committee provides promotional materials and produces subtitles and slogans, which are distributed to movie theaters in various places to be shown on the screen before the screening.

Rural Promotion

The fourth day is rural promotion. Those who are in charge on this day are the Farmers' Association, the Party Headquarters, and the Municipal Councilors in each district. The bureau convenes the Farmers' Association and the Municipal Councilors in advance to discuss and instruct the promotion policy. The principles are: (1) Formulate rural cooperative promotional materials and hand them over to the Municipal Councilors, Farmers' Association, and Party Headquarters in each district for distribution; (2) The Party Headquarters, the Municipal Councilors, and the Farmers' Association in each district are responsible, and the bureau's preparatory committee sends a letter to the Public Security Bureau, ordering the Public Security Bureau in each district to hold a masquerade parade on the morning of this day and asking the Public Security Bureau in each district to assist; (3) The Municipal Councilors, Farmers' Association, and Party Headquarters in each district are responsible for organizing cooperative promotion variety shows. On the afternoon of this day, appropriate locations are set up for masquerade performances.

School Promotion

The fifth day is school promotion. The Municipal Education Bureau orders various schools, summer schools, and literacy schools to hold lectures on cooperative promotion week at appropriate locations on this day and distribute promotional publications.

Labor Promotion

The sixth day is labor promotion. Those who are in charge on this day are the various trade unions. The bureau first convenes the persons in charge of the various trade unions to discuss the methods to be carried out. The principles are: (1) The preparatory committee prints various promotional materials suitable for workers and distributes them to the various trade unions in advance, instructing them to distribute them to various factories at the time; (2) At the convening of the discussion meeting, give a brief lecture on the principles to the representatives and instruct each trade union to nominate several people to prepare lecture materials in advance and give roving speeches to various factories; (3) The bureau nominates personnel to inspect the progress of the various large and small factories in each district on this day.

Closing Ceremony on the Seventh

The seventh day is the last day, holding the closing ceremony (no ceremony). Airplanes circle the city and distribute small slogans and leaflets. As for the promotion projects, there are five types: broadcasting, writing, variety shows, parades, and lectures. The broadcasting lecture materials are prepared by the broadcasters themselves. The preparatory committee provides the materials for the rhetoric, such as a simple introduction to cooperation and scripts. In terms of writing, in addition to the special issues published by the daily newspapers, the bureau publishes cooperative picture books and cooperative publications, which are distributed to various places. On the days of the promotion, the preparatory committee sends personnel to take photographs separately. The daily news is provided by the preparatory committee to the newspaper offices for publication.

Seamen's Organizations Oppose Salary Cuts; Shipping Guild Issues Statement Yesterday, Defending 20% Salary Reduction 103

According to the *Shen Shi News*, due to declining business and internal cost-cutting, the member companies of the Shanghai Shipping Guild recently decided to reduce the monthly salaries of seamen earning above 15 yuan by 20% starting from July 1st. Upon hearing this news, over a dozen seamen's organizations, including the Chinese Marine Engineers Association, the Chinese Captains Association, and the Wireless Operators Public Welfare Association, expressed deep dissatisfaction. They considered this decision to have a significant impact on the livelihoods of seamen and vehemently opposed it, issuing declarations accordingly. In addition, various sailors' organizations such as Yan Ying Nan She also unanimously issued urgent declarations, publicly announcing opposition to the salary cut. Simultaneously, they petitioned the Chinese Seamen's Party Branch to negotiate with the Shipping Guild to cancel the proposed plan. As of now, no substantial outcome has been achieved. It is now learned that the Shipping Guild, due to misunderstandings arising from a notice previously issued by the Chinese Marine Engineers Association and other organizations, also published a notice yesterday to inform all sectors, putting forward eight reasons and explaining their unavoidable hardship in temporarily paying 80% of salaries. The original text of their notice is as follows: Shanghai Shipping Guild Public Announcement. Having read the notice published by the Chinese Marine Engineers United Federation, the Chinese Merchant Marine Captains Federation, and the Chinese Ship Wireless Operators Public Welfare Association opposing seamen's salary cuts, we find much of the wording to be misleading. Our guild originally did not want to waste time on unnecessary arguments, but fearing that the outside world would be misled by a lack of understanding of the true situation, we hereby disclose the true facts to society. This time, our guild, based on a resolution of a temporary general meeting, due to industry decline and internal cost-cutting, has provisionally decided to pay 80% of the salaries of seamen earning over 15 yuan per month starting from July 1st of this year. This will be implemented at the discretion of each company. In addition to notifying member private companies, we also sincerely sent letters to relevant organizations. This demonstrates our spirit of mutual assistance. We endured the pain and temporarily accommodated the situation in order to avoid suspending operations and suffering the consequences. This was truly out of unavoidable hardship. These organizations hastily published large-scale notices, accusing private shipping businesses of extreme disregard. Whether there are other motives is obvious to discerning individuals. We now refute several points they made as follows: (1) Although there are rental fees for supplying military charters, it is a proven fact whether they are more profitable than regular business during peacetime. We believe that the pain is due to foreign ships monopolizing passenger and cargo transport during emergency periods. When Chinese ships are required for minimal chartering, in comparison, they cannot match the reliable schedules of foreign ships, thus being affected. (2) After September 18th, 40 ships were added. If all domestic goods were shipped by Chinese ships, the existing ships would be far from sufficient. After September 18th, our private shipping businesses attempted to recover rights and interests and had to make some preparations. We could not have foreseen that our countrymen would fail to sympathize, leading to the current even more difficult situation. Moreover, 19 of the added ships were acquired through emotional appeals and mortgages. There are also records in the Shipping Administration Bureau that can be checked. It should be known that among these 40 ships, several thousand seamen were able to find employment. Shipping merchants are struggling to support this, allowing thousands of seamen to have a livelihood. The so-called booming situation is perhaps reasonably spoken of by outsiders who are unaware of the situation, but it is unexpected to hear it from the mouths of seamen, and it contains a tone of blame. (3) Ships have a mobile nature, so they need to add fuel everywhere. Ships traveling to Southeast Asia can add Keelung coal, but ships in Shanghai must purchase domestic coal. Although coal prices are slightly lower than before, compared to freight revenue, it is not as sufficient as when coal prices were higher in the past. Even taking the Tianjin-Shanghai route as an example, the freight rate for flour is only 16 cents per dan, and the freight rate for coal is only 1.5 yuan per ton. There is also factual evidence to prove this. (4) Regarding seamen's salaries, the current salaries of Japanese ship captains are all between 200 and 250 Japanese yen per month, and even lower-level seamen are no less cheap, and all expenses are in Japanese yen. In comparison, the cost is 30-40% lower than Chinese ships. Since we cannot prevent cargo from being loaded onto Japanese ships, how can we compete with them? If we simply wait for death, if the skin does not exist, what will the hair adhere to? (5) The companies' overdue salaries are not due to a lack of funds to pay them. Can't the seamen see and hear this? This shows that the relationship between owners and employees has always been harmonious, and it also proves the actual economic difficulties. (6) The statement that if salaries are reduced by 20%, why not also reduce freight rates by 20% and clearly seek private gain is even more ridiculous. If the freight rate discount is used as the standard for salary reduction, then I am afraid it will be less than 50%. May we ask if these organizations can use this as the standard? (7) The statement that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has seen its business improve since it was nationalized after being in debt of hundreds of thousands of yuan is incorrect. This company is the only state-owned shipping company, and its situation is naturally different from that of private companies. Regardless of its superior pier facilities, may we ask if any commercial enterprise can indefinitely ignore the principal and interest on its debts? Moreover, with the government as its backing and priority for postal and joint transport, it is also heard that the government has advanced over 5 million yuan in the past three years. If private companies had the same treatment, they would not be in this situation. (8) National shipping is a plan set by the Premier, and rewarding and protecting private shipping is a provision stipulated in the Provisional Constitution. The two are not contradictory. If they say that the fundamental solution is to completely nationalize, shipping merchants would be willing if there is a reasonable price. As for the issue of issuing shipping public bonds, it has already been approved on file. As for its method, we do not expect government subsidies, but only to clear mortgages and circulate funds to seek survival for private shipping. If shipping merchants can survive, seamen's livelihoods can be stabilized. Only those who are insane or have ulterior motives would oppose it. We believe that the remaining aggressive personal remarks are the opinions of a few individuals, seeking momentary gratification, gloating, and disregarding the overall situation. We do not bother to argue. We solemnly declare that if these organizations have other remarks in the future, we will not respond. We hereby publish this announcement for your fair judgment.

China National Products Maintenance Association Promotes Commercial Acceptance Drafts; Submits a Petition to Government Authorities Requesting Issuance of a Proclamation to Promote Them 105

In order to promote commercial acceptance drafts to rescue domestic industry and commerce and stimulate social finance, the China National Products Maintenance Association, in addition to sending separate letters to member organizations and factories to encourage implementation, has also specifically submitted petitions to the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Headquarters, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, requesting the issuance of a proclamation to inform everyone to implement them together. The petition requests the publication of a notice to encourage factories and merchants to implement commercial acceptance drafts in order to rescue domestic products. It is submitted for the purpose of the petition. Commercial acceptance drafts can indeed revitalize the market and increase capital. Their contribution to the survival and development of domestic industry and commerce is by no means superficial. Therefore, since the implementation of the Negotiable Instruments Law, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the Silk Industry Guild, and other organizations have initiated their creation and implementation, and more and more parties are responding and imitating them. Since commercial acceptance drafts can be circulated in the market once signed by the acceptor, turning stagnant accounts receivable into active finance, and can also be discounted to banks and pawnshops before maturity, its effect is equivalent to cash. Not only does it actually increase the capital share of the market by tens of thousands, it can also reduce disputes, increase the credit of both parties, and expand the sales of goods. It is truly a good and beautiful method of killing several birds with one stone. There is no better way to rescue industry and commerce than this. Our domestic manufacturers, at a time when financial tensions and economic downturns are increasing day by day, should resolutely implement it to enrich capital and consolidate the foundation. However, there are often ignorant merchants who adhere to old habits and are reluctant to reform, strongly opposing it, resulting in the failure to widely implement it. The domestic industry is deeply distressed. The association, in order to promote this system and rescue commercial difficulties, in addition to issuing orders to member factories to quickly handle commercial acceptance drafts in accordance with the law, submits this petition to your esteemed government departments for inspection and approval. Please issue a proclamation and publish a notice clarifying the advantages and absence of disadvantages of this system, and urge everyone to implement it together, in order to rescue and maintain industry and commerce. We are extremely anxious to await orders, and we also pray for instructions to comply with them as a virtue.

Aviation Lottery to Promote Sales 109

The sales area for the National Government's Aviation Highway Construction Lottery has always been more than ten provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Sichuan, Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, Suiyuan, Henan, Shandong, and Hunan. Companies such as Dayun, Rongxin, and Yi Ji, as well as major banks, are entrusted to handle the business. It has recently been confirmed that the lottery office, in order to promote sales, has entrusted the central branch banks in Shaanxi, Gansu, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces to sell the lottery tickets, which will be handled by the central branch banks in each province. It is also heard that the Northeast and Southeast Asia are being promoted by Dayun and Guangxing companies, respectively. Furthermore, the new method of changing the ticket amount, prize amount, and shortening the prize draw period of the office will be implemented from the 13th issue. All methods for the 12th issue of lottery tickets, which will be drawn on July 5th, will remain completely unchanged. The first prize will still be 500,000 yuan.

After the police station obtained the confession, they arrested the related parties on the 22nd and sent a judicial officer to Shanghai to surround Matsubara & Co. on Wuzhou Road, arresting Matsubara's cousin, an employee of a certain company named Suzuki, and many other suspects.

Traditional Chinese Medicine Registration; Can Register Directly with the Health Bureau; No Need to Entrust Any Organization to Forward to Avoid Complications 117

Registration for traditional Chinese medicine practitioners in Shanghai this year has already started on June 1st. All unregistered and unapproved traditional Chinese medicine practitioners in the city can directly go to the bureau within the time limit to register in accordance with the regulations. The procedures are extremely simple and do not require introduction and forwarding by any organization. It is also heard that all those who apply for traditional Chinese medicine registration, in addition to paying the registration fee of four yuan, the license fee of three yuan, and the stamp tax of one yuan at the time of registration in accordance with the regulations, there are no other fees. Those who fail the examination in the future can also get a refund of the license fee and stamp tax by presenting the registration receipt. However, the registration fee will not be refunded in accordance with the regulations. It is hoped that all traditional Chinese medicine practitioners in the city will pay attention.

Guanghua Medical Journal Advocates Cooperation Between Chinese and Western Medicine 118

The *Guanghua Medical Journal*, located at No. 9 Difeng Li, North Shaanxi Road, Shanghai, has been publishing a monthly magazine for two years. European and American countries pay special attention to them. China's medicine and pharmaceuticals have a history of thousands of years. Not only has medicine and pharmaceuticals not progressed, but they have also fallen into a chaotic situation, which is truly heartbreaking. The journal believes that academics have no borders and that one should choose the good and follow it. Chinese and Western medicine each have their own advantages and disadvantages. It strives to eliminate prejudices, cooperate, and research with each other, and should take the entire field of medicine and pharmaceuticals as a prerequisite.

Taxpayers' Association Asks Municipal Council to Pay Attention to the Interests of Telephone Users; Lists Five Points to Order the Company to Correct Immediately 119

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: Dear Sirs, regarding the telephone incident, please order the Shanghai Telephone Company to make corrections in accordance with the powers conferred by the taxpayers in order to protect the interests of taxpayer users. (1) Although the telephone fee has been changed from payment every three months to payment every month, the payment period should still be after monthly use. (2) Telephone fees should be calculated on a monthly basis. For example, from the beginning of the month to the end of the month, the company should calculate any fractions. Each machine should not collect an improper gain of five days per year. (3) The retroactive temporary surcharge for April and May should be calculated from the date of installation for telephones installed only in May or from April 2nd. Otherwise, it will be an extra-legal income. (4) To speak with the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, it must not be transferred without the user's written notification and registration. There must also be a confirmed registration method to avoid unfair facts such as charging the wrong person, where some users do not pay and others who do not use the service are charged. (5) There are many errors in this telephone directory. In order to protect the legitimate interests of users, the company should reprint and distribute it according to the previous method of the China and Foreign Telephone Company. A corresponding letter is hereby sent. We hope you will investigate and handle it.

Radio Broadcasting Stations Broadcast Record Issues, International Phonograph Association Demands Fee Payment, Monthly Fee of One Hundred and Fifty Dollars Required 123

According to the Great American Evening Post, there are no less than sixty radio broadcasting stations in Shanghai. Besides broadcasting live singing and storytelling, they also play phonograph records. Various record companies have found that since broadcasting stations play their records, residents purchase fewer records, which greatly affects their business. Therefore, the International Phonograph Industrial Federation has commissioned Mr. Watson, the manager of the Shanghai Electrical Music Company, to write to various broadcasting stations, stating that from July 1st, anyone broadcasting records must pay a monthly fee of one hundred and fifty dollars, or legal action will be taken. It is said that recently the British court heard a similar lawsuit, and the plaintiff won. According to the current situation, most of the Shanghai broadcasting stations are run by Chinese and have limited capital and small scale, they would have no ability to pay this fee. Even the broadcasting stations run by foreigners, their current income is also small, it is feared that they will not be able to pay this huge fee every month.

Contemporary Literary Giant Zeng Mengpu Passes Away from Illness, Tired of Politics, He Retired to the Countryside, His Lifelong Writings Reached Over One Hundred Volumes 124

Zeng Mengpu of Changshu, pen name "Sick Man of East Asia," father of Mr. Zeng Xubai, the chief editor of the Da Wan Bao, passed away from illness at his hometown on the afternoon of the twenty-third of this month. Mr. Zeng was learned and virtuous, a politician and a literary figure of his time. Now he has suddenly passed away, those who knew him and those who did not, all express their condolences. Here is a summary of his life facts:

Mr. Mengpu was sixty-five years old. During the late Qing Dynasty, he passed the Jinshi examination. In the early Republic, he successively served as a member of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly, Secretary-General of the Jiangsu Provincial Governor's Office, Director of the Jiangsu Public Property Administration Office, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, Director of the Department of Administration, Acting Governor, and other positions. Later, administrative affairs became increasingly busy, which caused him to fall ill. Therefore, in 1925, he decided to abandon everything, recuperate in Shanghai, and engage in writing. During the Guangxu era, he initially founded the Xiaoshelin Bookstore. In 1926, he reopened the Zhenmei Bookstore, planning and managing it diligently. It was an expression of his lifelong dedication to literary pursuits. He wrote poetry, essays, notes, textual research, plays, novels, and other works, totaling over one hundred volumes, and was a giant in contemporary literary circles. The widely popular novels "A Flower in a Sea of Sin" and "The Man from Lu" are his carefully crafted masterpieces. In recent years, his physical strength declined, so he returned to his hometown to recuperate. At the foot of the mountain, he built a villa called "Xuzai Residence." He personally planted every flower and tree in the garden and devoted himself to the study of botany, gaining considerable insights. Recently, Mr. Zeng's illness suddenly worsened, and medical treatment was ineffective. On the afternoon of the twenty-third, amidst the bleak wind and rain, he passed away. All who heard the news could not help but feel grief and shed tears.

Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society, Content and Organization Updated, Municipal Council Chairman Arnold Returns to England 125

The issue of reforming the Public Concession Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society once caused disputes last month. The Municipal Council, therefore, set up a special committee on rickshaws, to jointly study and handle the matter with the Rickshaw Affairs Management Committee. At the meeting of the Municipal Council Board of Directors, the special committee submitted a report stating that since its establishment, the society had held two meetings. The first was preliminary in nature, and the second discussed the organizational methods of the mutual aid fund management committee and the board of directors. According to the agreement in August last year, the organization of the Mutual Aid Society was for a trial period of eight months. Now that the term has expired, the rickshaw owners have been strenuously advocating for reorganization. According to the special committee's proposal, the organization of the management committee and the board of directors will be stipulated as follows: (1) The fund management committee will have three members, one from the Rickshaw Committee, one representative from the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, who should be a member of the Chamber of Commerce, and one representative from the Chinese Ratepayers Association, who should be a respected banker in the city. (2) The board of directors will consist of three members of the Rickshaw Committee, two representatives of registered rickshaw owners, two representatives of registered rickshaw pullers (subject to the approval of the board of directors after the organization of their election body), one member of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, one member of the Chinese Ratepayers Association, and four social workers. Previously, the fund management committee had three members, all of whom were members of the Rickshaw Committee. Now, one local impartial businessman and one banker will each serve as members to show fairness and impartiality. Furthermore, the original board of directors had twelve seats, with three members from the Rickshaw Committee, two representatives of rickshaw owners, and seven social workers. Although there was a provision for two seats for rickshaw pullers, no representatives were ever elected, which was tantamount to giving up their rights. Now, the number of social workers has been reduced to four, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Ratepayers Association will each elect one person to participate, also to demonstrate the principle of impartiality. If the Board of Directors approves the special committee's proposal, the new members of the management committee must wait until the existing committee submits its accounts before they can take office. At the board of directors meeting, the proposed organizational rules for the fund management committee and the board of directors, suggested by the special committee, have been generally approved. However, regarding the social workers on the board of directors, it was decided to reduce the number from four to three. Furthermore, all rickshaw puller representative positions on the board of directors should be held by rickshaw pullers. Furthermore, Mr. Arnold, the chairman of the Municipal Council, left Shanghai today (the 25th) to return to England on official business and is expected to return around September 4th. During Mr. Arnold's vacation, the duties of the chairman will be temporarily assumed by the vice-chairman, Mr. Lamb.

Dispute Between Elementary School Principal and Female Teacher, They Lived Together and Had a Daughter, After Separation, Lawsuits Continued - The Case of Returning the Girl Was Finally Resolved 126

Chen Ziying, a 23-year-old woman from Songjiang, was introduced to Jinghua Elementary School on Tangshan Road in 1933 by the brother of Wu Yao, the principal of the school, who was from Wuxian County, to work as a teacher. Therefore, she and Wu Yao spent time together day and night, and soon engaged in physical relations. They rented a house at 111 Fuzhi Road in the French Concession and lived together. At that time, Chen did not know that Wu was already married. When she learned that Wu had married Cao as his wife, their relationship broke down. As a result of negotiations, they announced their separation on October 10th. At that time, Chen was already several months pregnant, so the contract stipulated that in addition to Wu paying Chen three thousand dollars in alimony, regardless of whether Chen gave birth to a boy or a girl, Chen would have custody, and Wu would pay ten dollars per month for support until the child reached the age of sixteen. From then on, they went their separate ways. Later, Chen gave birth to a daughter named Xuerong on February 6th of this year. Because she did not have milk, she entrusted the child to Wu's sister, Wu Yueying. Recently, Chen filed a lawsuit against Wu Yao in the civil court of the First Special District Court for failing to fulfill the contract. The case had already been heard once and was rescheduled for the fourteenth of this month. Chen was beaten when she went to Wu's house to pick up Xuerong. She reported the incident to the Huishan Police Station and sued Wu for assault in the First Special District Court. After interrogation, Wu was fined fifteen yuan as a warning. Before one wave subsided, another rose. Chen Ziying is now suing Wu Yao, Wu Yueying, and Wu Cao for jointly abusing Xuerong maliciously, not feeding her milk, and causing her to become seriously ill. She believes that the reason for this is that they intend to cause the child's death to avoid paying the ten dollars per month in support. She considers it malicious abandonment and has retained lawyer Yang Zhenxiong to sue Wu Yueying, Wu Yao, and Wu Cao for abandonment in the criminal court of the First Special District Court, requesting that they be charged with the crime of abandonment, and as part of the civil lawsuit, she demands the return of Xuerong. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi opened the third criminal court to summon the defendants. Wu Yueying did not appear due to illness. All others arrived on time. First, Chen Ziying stated the course of events. The judge then asked if her purpose was only to have Xuerong returned, and if Xuerong could be returned, whether she would withdraw the lawsuit. Chen said that if the child could be returned, she would withdraw the lawsuit. When questioned, Wu Yao agreed to return Xuerong to Chen, stating that the reason why he did not return the child immediately when the civil court opened was that the plaintiff had not acknowledged all the expenses for the child from February 6th to the present. Now he is willing to return the child immediately. Judge Jiang, seeing that the case had been settled, had both parties sign the document and ruled that the case was not accepted.

Grand Performance of "Red Mane Stallion" at the Universal Art Theater Today, Accompanied by Percussion and Wind Instruments, Xiao Fei Orchestra and Thai Music 128

The Universal Art Theater, founded by Song Chunfang and Mrs. France, is staging the complete Chinese opera "Red Mane Stallion" for the first time, in full traditional costume, with English dialogue. It is scheduled to premiere today at 9 PM at the Carlton Theater at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Baker Road, with another performance tomorrow. Due to requests from various parties to extend the run, it has been decided to continue the performance for three days. The performance program is as follows:

Musical Atmosphere: Chinese opera percussion is the main musical instrument. In this performance of "Red Mane Stallion", it was originally intended not to use percussion in order to make it more modern. However, as a result of the dress rehearsal, it was felt that Chinese opera relied on body movements and steps, which could not be coordinated without percussion. Therefore, it has been decided to use percussion. In addition, there will be pipa, phoenix flute, erhu, yangqin, etc. The Xiao Fei Orchestra will perform "Neon Clothes Song," "Early Thunder," "Buddha Ascending the Hall" (flute solo), "Bawang Unloading Armor" (pipa solo), "Pu'an Mantra," and five other pieces. The stage set and costumes are contracted by Shanghai's most famous Xu Pinji, the full set of costumes will be rich and beautiful.

Cast: The play has a total of thirty-three actors, including many famous actors, such as Tang Ying, Ling Xianyang, and Mrs. Song Wenbin, who are quite well-known. Zhang Taihao and Zhang Taizhen are the daughters of an ambassador. Ni Xuanqing, Zhai Guanliang, etc. once went to the United States with Mei Lanfang to perform. The successful performance of this play is not accidental. Below is a survey of the main actors: Fang Bofen plays Prime Minister Wang Yun, Wei Zutong plays the Prime Minister's wife, Ni Xuanqing plays Wei Hu, Huang Xuanping plays Su Long, Lei Ruijin plays Wang Jinchuan (Su Long's wife), Guo Wanying plays Wang Yinchuan (Wei Hu's wife), Tang Ying plays Tu Baochuan, Ling Xianyang plays Xue Pinggui, Wang Shuying plays the old man, Song Wenbin plays Princess Daizhan of Western Liang, and more than twenty other people. Ren Shuying and Ms. Xiao Su will direct. The eight acts of the play are a combination of the English translation by Xiong Shiyi and the Chinese script.

Program Description: The eight acts of the play are based on a combination of Xiong Shiyi's English translation and the Chinese script. The plot has some differences from the traditional opera. The acts are described as follows: Act 1 "Wang Yun Appreciates Snow" (not in the traditional opera) Prime Minister Wang Yun advises his daughter Wang Baochuan to marry. There are many young masters and princes who are entangled in courtship, but Baochuan appreciates the talented Xue Pinggui, believing that he will achieve great things in the future. She has already promised herself to him. Therefore, she decides to choose a husband by throwing a silk ball. Act 2 "Throwing the Silk Ball" On February 2nd, Baochuan throws the silk ball to choose a husband. Pinggui is nearby, and the ball accidentally hits him. Act 3 "Three Slaps" Baochuan insists on marrying Pinggui, but Wang Yun does not agree, and the father and daughter break up. After three slaps, Baochuan leaves the prime minister's mansion with Pinggui to live in a humble abode. Act 4 "Joining the Army and Bidding Farewell" Pinggui joins the army and is about to go to Western Liang, saying a tearful farewell to his wife Baochuan. Act 5 "Passing Three Barriers" Eighteen years later, Pinggui has married Princess Daizhan in Western Liang and succeeded to the throne. One day, he accidentally remembers his ex-wife Baochuan in the cold kiln, so he abandons his wealth and leaves without saying goodbye. Princess Daizhan discovers this and rushes out of the three barriers, intending to chase him back. After Pinggui explains, he obtains the princess's understanding, allowing Pinggui to return home. Act 6 "Wu Jia Po" Pinggui returns to Wu Jia Po to test his wife, knowing that Baochuan has maintained her chastity for eighteen years, her character is steadfast. After a long separation, they meet again, filled with sorrow and joy. Act 7 "Calculating Grain in the Prime Minister's Mansion," Act 8 "Grand Enthronement Ceremony" Pinggui becomes the master of Western Liang and has a grand reunion with Baochuan and Princess Daizhan.

Fisherman in a Panic After Catching a Dead Body in His Net, Knife Wounds Discovered on the Body 130

There is a river called DachiTou south of Min'an Road on North Baoxing Road, Zhabei, not far from Mingqiang Middle School. The river is rich in fish, so most of the residents nearby are fishing families and make a living by fishing. At dawn yesterday, eight or nine fishermen from the area went to the DachiTou River to set nets and fish, preparing to sell their catch in the vegetable market. Not long after setting the nets, the fishermen felt that the bottom of the net was unusually heavy. They all thought that a huge fish had been caught in the net and were overjoyed. They hurriedly pulled up the net, but upon closer inspection, their faces turned pale. What was in the net was not a fish, but a corpse. The fishermen were immediately panicked and did not know what to do. Fortunately, an elder was slightly more composed and immediately ran to report to the nearby Baziqiao Branch. The patrol officer of the branch led a senior police officer to investigate. Indeed, it was a male corpse, with a lifelike face, about twenty years old, wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, barefoot and bald, with his mouth and eyes not closed. Several knife wounds were found on his body. Having been in the water for too long, it had already started to decompose, and the abdomen was bulging like a giant stone. After questioning the neighbors, no one recognized the body. It was thought that he was killed and thrown into the river. The patrol officer then reported to the Baoshan Road Branch, and the district chief Fu Chu went to investigate in person, ordering the local security officer to report to the local court that afternoon to request an autopsy and also report to the bureau to investigate the case and search for relatives to claim the body.

Animal Protection Society Sends a Letter Requesting the Prohibition of Catching Non-Venomous Green Snakes, Beggars Play with Snakes to Beg for Sale in an Extremely Cruel Manner, It Is Requested to Investigate and Prohibit Them at Any Time to Stop the Cruel Practices 135

The China Animal Protection Society recently sent a letter to the Hangzhou Municipal Government yesterday regarding the fact that beggars in Hangzhou were catching non-venomous green snakes to make a living, requesting them to order the Public Security Bureau to investigate and prohibit them at any time in order to stop the cruel practices. The details are as follows:

Beggars in Hangzhou Catch Snakes to Make a Profit

Philanthropist Zhu Yinjiang wrote to the society, saying that he wanted to address the fact that beggars in Hangzhou were catching green snakes to make a profit. He said, "I was in Hangzhou before and saw many snake-playing beggars who specialize in catching non-venomous green snakes and selling them along the road in front of temples, persuading people to buy and release them, calling it a good deed, but it is actually a scam. After people buy and release them, the next day they catch the released snakes again and sell them again, catching and releasing them repeatedly to make a profit. Those who sincerely release animals are causing these innocent animals to suffer more pain, not being able to live or die. The cruelty is beyond words. I have always admired your society for protecting animals and sparing no effort. Can you send a letter to the local Public Security Bureau ordering the police to prohibit beggars from catching snakes? It is appropriate to ask your society to ask the philanthropists to discuss in detail to stop this practice, which would be a great benefit."

Letter to the Hangzhou Municipal Government Ordering Investigation and Prohibition

After receiving the report, the society, represented by Chairman Ye Gongchuo and Vice Chairman Guan Jiongzhi, sent a letter to the Hangzhou Municipal Government yesterday, saying: "We are writing to you because Mr. Zhu Yinjiang, a member of our society, wrote to us, saying that in Hangzhou, he saw snake-playing beggars who specialize in catching non-venomous green snakes and selling them along the road in front of temples, persuading people to buy and release them. After people buy snakes and release them, these beggars catch them again and sell them again, calling it a good deed, but it is actually a scam, and it causes innocent animals to suffer repeatedly. He asked us to forward a letter requesting investigation and prohibition. The act of beggars playing with snakes to beg for sale is extremely cruel and easily leads to cruel practices. We are sending you this letter to request that you order the Public Security Bureau to investigate and prohibit them at any time in order to eliminate fraud and cruel practices. We look forward to hearing from you."

Re-Trial of Li Guocheng, Who Was Sentenced to Death: Returned by Higher Court; Essential Witnesses Still to Be Called 136

On the afternoon of August 15th, Year 20 of the Republic of China, at approximately 6:00 PM, a case occurred at No. 2 room of the Fa Shang (法商) Hotel, located at No. 113 West Xinqiao Street in the French Concession. Within, Jiangbei bandits, Lei He Can (類和殘), shot and killed Xia Yongsheng, Jiang Zhonghan, a Mr. Xue, and thirteen others, and wounded Zhong Ziqing. The French police apprehended the suspect, Yan Jinbiao from Funing, and Yan Yi, on the following day and handed them over to the court. After the court concluded the trial, they were sentenced to death. During the trial, Yan confessed that Li Guocheng, also known as Chen You, instigated him, assembling Jiu Cheng (九成), Liu Wu (劉五), Zhang San (張三), and others who were at large to go and commit the murders. Subsequently, based on information from Yan's family, Li was apprehended in the Rihui Port area of Shanghai South and sent to the Public Security Bureau. A request was made to the First Special District Court to bring him to trial. The court ordered the police to investigate and prosecute. After the trial concluded, Li Guocheng was also sentenced to death. Immediately the criminal was sentenced to death according to law. Li refused to accept the original verdict and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, but the appeal was rejected. Li still refused to accept the verdict and filed a third appeal with the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court, after reviewing the entire case file, noted that when Jiang Zhonghan, a victim, was questioned at Renji Hospital after Yan was apprehended, he stated that he only recognized three of the perpetrators and that Li Guocheng was only implicated by Yan's confession. There was no concrete evidence to prove whether Li actually went to commit the murders, so further investigation was deemed necessary. Therefore, the Supreme Court decided to overturn the original verdict and return the case to the Third Branch of the High Court for a new trial. The Second Branch of the High Court received the returned case file, and the presiding judge, Guo Dezhang, together with assessors Xiong and Zhu, and prosecutor Zhang, held a re-trial the day before yesterday. Li Guocheng's defense lawyer, Zhang Shijie, and others were also present in court awaiting instructions. Qian Yumin, the detective from the French police who handled the case, was also summoned to the court to be questioned. The court first questioned the appellant, Li Guocheng, who continued to deny participating in the murders, claiming that Yan Jinbiao was holding a grudge and falsely implicated him. He requested that the truth be revealed. Then, Detective Qian Yumin testified about the circumstances under which he apprehended Yan and the victims' identification of the perpetrators at Renji Hospital. Later, the court determined that a key witness in the case, Wang Jiemei, the manager of the Fa Shang Hotel, had not been summoned to court. Therefore, the court adjourned the trial and decided to summon the witness to court for further questioning at a later date, and then adjourned.

### Wang Yangshan Accused of Disrupting Family: Taking a Chang Sister as a Concubine; Older Sister Files Suit After Her Uncle's Accusation 137

Wang Yangshan, a native of Zhenjiang and assistant manager of the Chengzihhao branch of the Huianli business located at the intersection of Hankou Road and Fujian Road, is 45 years old. Previously, because his wife had been unable to bear children for a long time, for continuation, he took a Chang woman from his hometown as a concubine in the fifteenth year. She soon gave birth to a daughter, who is now eight years old. Last year, the concubine's father died in their hometown. The concubine, feeling that her three brothers were useless and fearing that her younger sister, Chang Rongzhen, would have difficulty making a living in their hometown, brought her to Shanghai to live with her. At that time, Rongzhen was only seventeen or eighteen years old. Although she was a country girl, she was quite beautiful. Wang Yangshan took a special liking to her and treated her extraordinarily well. By the end of January last year, Wang, using the excuse that neither his wife nor concubine had given birth to a son, expressed his unresolved anxieties and wished to take another concubine in the hope of fulfilling his long-cherished desire. The concubine had long suspected Wang's intentions and felt that Rongzhen was also suitable to bear a son. Therefore, imitating the story of the sisters Ehuang and Nüying, they both served Wang together. From then on, Wang enjoyed the pleasures of being surrounded by beautiful women. Unexpectedly, the concubine, after offering her sister to Wang, suddenly resented that Wang's favor was not evenly distributed and that she was not treated equally. Consequently, her attitude also changed, and she gradually became romantic and engaged in illicit behavior with other men. Because the matter was not kept secret, Wang eventually discovered it. Wang took decisive action and drew up an agreement to permanently sever their relationship. The concubine's younger brother, Chang Rongpei, who had been living and eating at Wang's house as the concubine's brother, left with his sister even though his younger sister remained because he did not get along with the younger sister. Currently, Chang Rongpei has hired a lawyer to sue Wang Yangshan in the First Special District Court for disrupting the family and other charges, requesting that Wang be punished in accordance with Article 257 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide opened the court to hear the case. First, the plaintiff, Chang Rongpei, stated the circumstances under which the defendant, Wang Yangshan, and his sisters separated, saying that Wang harmed his sister and also committed adultery with his younger sister, and denied that his sister and Wang were concubines, and that he had agreed. Next, Wang Yangshan stated that taking Rongzhen as a concubine was entirely advocated by her sister, and that he had even hosted a banquet at the time. Chang Rongzhen also surrendered to the court, saying that she lived with Wang on the orders of her sister, and that the plaintiff knew everything beforehand. Finally, the witnesses invited by the defendant testified that Wang hosted a banquet when he took a concubine, and that they were invited guests. Judge Feng then adjourned the hearing until the morning of the 29th of this month for further questioning.

Small Steamer Collides with Ferry, Two Ferry Passengers Fall into River 139

There was originally a ferryboat at Dongjiadu in the southern section of the Huangpu River, carrying passengers back and forth between the west bank of Puxi and the east bank of Pudong. The captain of the ferryboat was Yang Jinsong. Yesterday morning at 6:30 AM, the ferryboat was carrying more than twenty passengers from Puxi to Pudong when a small steamer from the Qiuxin Factory, traveling north from the south, approached midstream. Due to the recent mooring of many dredgers in the area, it approached the ferryboat too closely, and it was too late to avoid a collision. The steamer collided with the ferryboat, and the ferryboat was shaken. Three villagers were shaken and fell into the Huangpu River. The steamer immediately stopped and began searching. One person was rescued on the spot, but the other two were missing. It was reported that the missing villagers were selling pickled vegetables, and their names were not yet known.

Additional news: The passengers who fell into the river were Tang Shutao and He Mulin. Afterwards, Qian, the wife of the deceased Tang Shutao, and Sheng, the mother of He Mulin, went to the Tangqiao police station in Pudong to request an investigation. According to Qian, her husband was 31 years old and lived in Tangjiazhai in Pudong. This morning, he went to Puxi to purchase funeral supplies for a relative, but unfortunately, he met with disaster on his way home. Her grief was overwhelming. According to Sheng, her son was 28 years old, a local resident living in Hejiazhai in Pudong. He went to Puxi this morning to buy pickled vegetables and was tragically knocked into the river and drowned. She requested justice. Sheng is already 60 years old and was sobbing uncontrollably as she spoke, her old tears streaming down her face. The director of the Dongjiadu station ordered that Yang A-Da, the ferryboat crew member responsible for the accident, be brought to the station for a brief interrogation before being sent to the general office for disposal. Yang Zhufa, another crew member, was summoned by the water patrol team for interrogation. As of last night, the bodies of the deceased had not yet been recovered.

Robbery in Dongbaiyang Lane Yesterday Morning 140

At 8:30 yesterday morning, four robbers broke into the home of Yao Jiangtian, a local resident who manages rentals at No. 3 Yangyinli, Dongbaiyang Lane, Zhonghua Road, Dananmen, Nanshi (a single-story stone gate house). A water company bill collector, Chen, went to Yao's house to collect the water bill. Yao invited Chen inside and asked him to wait in the parlor while Yao went upstairs to the writing room on the upper floor to write a bank check. Suddenly, they heard a knock on the door. Yao's widowed sister-in-law opened the door, and four robbers rushed in. They first approached Chen and asked if he was Mr. Yao. Chen replied that Mr. Yao was upstairs. Upon hearing this, the robbers showed their guns and ordered them to be silent. They then began their robbery, with one robber guarding the front door and another searching Chen's wallet. Two other robbers went upstairs and saw Yao Jiangquan writing a check. They threatened him with their guns, saying, "Please help us out." They then opened the wallet on the desk and took more than a hundred yuan in cash. Still not satisfied, they turned and went to the front building. Yao's wife heard the sound of the robbery and remained silent in fear, allowing the robbers to ransack the cabinets. In total, they stole more than 800 yuan in cash and a gold ring from Yao's wife's finger (weighing six qian). After obtaining the loot, the robbers forced Yao and his wife downstairs and into the back of the parlor, ordering them to stand facing the wall, not to look back, and not to cross the line. The robbers then rushed out the door and fled. Afterwards, Yao Jiangtian and Chen reported the incident to the local police station and requested an investigation. Jin Dianyang, the station chief, immediately ordered the officers to search the area, but the robbers had already disappeared. The four robbers were well-dressed. One wore a blue silk gauze long gown, was about 30 years old, and wore a straw hat. Another wore a dark Indian silk long gown and a felt hat, and was about 30 years old. One wore a gray Indian silk long gown, was bald, and had no hat, and was about 40 years old. One wore a white silk short shirt and pants, and was about 20 years old. They all spoke with a local accent and carried guns. Yao Jiangtian's family is not wealthy, and the stolen money was rent collected on behalf of others. He is now lamenting the loss of the large sum of money.

A Description of the Grand Fish Banquet at Guanshengyuan Farm 155

The Guanshengyuan Farm in Caohejing invited people from the literary and art circles, fish artists, and the film industry in Shanghai to view the goldfish and tour the farm the day before yesterday (Sunday), and prepared a grand banquet. Proof from the Association for the Promotion of National Goods: Registration of the Lihua Weaving Factory Trademark 156

Shanghai citizens advocate for national goods. According to a report from the factory member, Lihua Weaving Factory, to ensure the tax amount of its products, it went to the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau to register. However, a trademark with the same name had already been registered, which infringed upon the right of the Ministry of Industry to register its trademark. It requested assistance. Yesterday, the Executive Committee decided to issue a letter of proof, along with various registration licenses, requesting approval of the registration to protect its legal rights. The letter is recorded below: "To whom it may concern, our factory member, Lihua Weaving Factory, has reported that its products, such as undershirts, require the use of unified tax forms. The factory sent personnel to the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau to declare and register. It was informed that a trademark with the same name had already been approved, and the requested registration was not permitted. Our member's trademark was approved by the Ministry of Industry on August 9th, 1932 and is duly registered. Therefore, we are writing to your association to forward this letter to the bureau, requesting that the registration be approved." After investigation, the member was granted Business Registration License No. 4821 by the Ministry of Industry, entitling it to all legal rights. Therefore, we are enclosing copies of the business license and trademark registration certificate, requesting your esteemed bureau to approve the registration. We hope for your favorable consideration.

Abducted Girl Sent to Bureau for Care 158

The day before yesterday afternoon, a lost girl wearing a fashionable watch, a purple floral calico jacket and pants, black thread socks, and blue cloth shoes was found lost in Longhua. A police officer spotted her and immediately took her back to the station. After questioning by Chief Wu, she said her name was Yi Xiang, eleven years old, from Yin Jiafang, Forty Tu, Shangrao, Jiangxi Province. Her mother was sick and went out to get medicine. She was abducted to Shanghai by Tang Lao Guan, who runs an inn. Her brother-in-law, Chen Zhenhao, works at the Shanghai airport. The girl had a leather bag, a powder box, six corner notes from Jiangxi Province, a small mirror, a photo of the child, a watch repair ticket, ten cents in stamps, and a cigarette card with medicine names written on it. Yesterday, a document was prepared and sent to the relief section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for care, pending family claiming her.

These two important resolutions were announced to all teams today, and the full schedule, team rosters, and match report forms were sent to each team separately. Teams that do not receive these documents within three days can contact Secretary Lu to obtain them, in order to avoid delaying the competition.

Chinese Table Tennis Association Requests Table Tennis to be Included in the National Games 163

Committee members Xu Duo, Hu Jiankun, Lu Zhongqiu, Lu Xiulu, and Chen Linsheng of the Chinese Table Tennis Association, because the Sixth National Games are about to be held in Shanghai, table tennis comrades heard this news and came to the association one after another to request sending a letter to the National Games to add table tennis championships. Mr. Xu and others believe that this matter is of great importance to the future of table tennis and went to Wang Bohong, Wang Mengnian, Zhang Yongren, Yang Xiqing and other gentlemen to seek opinions, and invited Wang Yi and others from the Chinese Table Tennis Research Association to participate in serious discussions. After several consultations, the draft was finally completed. It is heard that in addition to the letter, the association also plans to push Xu Duo, Yu Binqi, Lu Zhongqiu, Hu Jiankun, and Chen Linsheng to take charge of the process and strive to achieve the goal. The full letter is recorded below, hoping that table tennis comrades from all over the country will rise up and strive for it together.

Respected Sirs, we rely on your efforts to organize this National Games. Your talents and plans are thorough and meticulous. Our association is deeply grateful for the future of the sports world. Now, there is a suggestion that table tennis has a long history and special functions. After several improvements, it has become a scientific sport. It is very developed in various countries and we should catch up quickly in our country. As far as our association can see, we believe that this National Games should officially include table tennis in the championship competition to promote it. We dare to offer our opinions, hoping that you will consider them and adopt them. (1) The progress of sports technology depends entirely on social promotion, and public awards are especially important. This can be seen from the past. Since the establishment of the National Government, it has made every effort to advocate national sports, and as a result, all sports have made great progress. If the government had seen this earlier and taken the lead, the results would be even better and would be able to compete with the world. Table tennis is a modern sport. Governments of various countries have promoted it vigorously. International competitions are held regularly. Our country lags behind in everything. After nearly 20 years of efforts by our association, we are fortunate to have achieved some results. If we can get your advocacy in this National Games and set up championships and include them in the competition, then there will be widespread response, and the results can be expected. In the future, we will also be able to cope with international competitions with ease. This is the first reason why table tennis should be included in the National Games Championship.

(2) Chairman Chiang issued a winter telegram to the whole country to exercise the national physique and transform the sound nation, requiring everyone to choose a sport and practice it regularly every day, even in wind, rain, ice and snow. The law is good and the meaning is beautiful. All nationals should abide by it. And to seek a sport, which is beneficial to individuals in terms of motivation, time, and place, and can achieve results soon, only table tennis is the easiest to practice, and it is the most consistent with the spirit of Chairman Chiang's perseverance in wind, rain, ice and snow. This is the second reason why table tennis should be included in the National Games Championship.

(3) It is said that this National Games has rumors of including shuttlecock and other games in the competition. If this is the case, table tennis, as a world-recognized scientific sport technology, should not be absent. This is the third reason why table tennis should be included in the National Games.

(4) Table tennis competitions have been included in the Far East Games as a performance, and there have been proposals to set up championships. The world table tennis competition is also very fierce. If we do not prepare early and train a strong army, it will be difficult to win once we join the competition. Today, we should prepare early so that we can be sharp when the time comes. This is the fourth reason why table tennis should be included in the National Games Championship. (To be continued)

Weiming was led by Emperor Jin Yan, and Telecom was led by Zhou Can. When the bell rang ten times, referee Chang Su Shao struck the silver horn, and the two teams began to fight. Brief Table of Literacy Rates among Overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies: Female Education is Particularly Backward 169

(Soviet News Agency, Batavia Correspondence) The literacy rates among overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies, according to the results of the 1920 census by the Census Bureau, are extracted and listed below in a detailed report on the literacy rates of overseas Chinese. Percentage of Literate People

From China Overseas Born

Men Women Men Women

Java and Madura 58.4 9.3 64.6 24.3

Sumatra 33.3 3.8 46.1 11.6

Other Outer Islands 57.2 6.8 60.4 18.5

The above table lists those aged nine and above. Those whose ages were unknown are omitted. Those whose ages were unknown accounted for about 15% of the total population, and very few of them were literate. Also, not many of those over 50 were literate. More overseas-born Chinese were literate. Very few women were literate. Also, the term "literate" in the table does not refer to Chinese, as those who were literate in English, Dutch, or Malay are also considered literate.

Spring Conference of the China Language Society Held in Tokyo: Professor Zhang Shilu from Jinan University Specially Invited to Give a Lecture, Dajima Denji Greatly Praises Zhang's Works 172

The China Language Society held its spring conference at the Kasumigaseki Hall at 2-2-4, Kasumigaseki, Kojimachi, Tokyo, at 1:00 PM on the 21st of this month. In addition to reporting on administrative matters and tasks, the conference invited Professor Zhang Shilu of Jinan University to give a lecture. The topics of the lecture were: (1) The Chinese Phonological System, (2) The Characteristics of the Chinese Language, and (3) The Trends in the Evolution of the Chinese Language and Literature. After the lecture, a dinner was held at 6:00 PM, followed by a discussion. When notifying the members in advance, the society introduced Zhang Shilu as follows: "Professor Zhang Shilu of the National Jinan University in Zhenru, Shanghai, is a famous Chinese linguist and phonologist. His works include Principles of Linguistics, Introduction to Linguistics, Outline of Linguistics, Phonology, Ancient Chinese Phonology, Essentials of Chinese Sound History, A Study of the Guangyun, and On the Evolution of Chinese Literature and Art. He recently translated the book Chinese Language and Chinese Writing by the Swedish phonologist Karlgren and published it. Dr. Dajima Masatake, a Japanese literary scholar, after reading Zhang's A Study of the Guangyun, praised it, saying that this work has the value of a doctoral dissertation."

Middle School Physical Education Teachers' Joint Examination - First Day, Director Pan Personally Inspects, Excellent Order in All Examination Venues 174

The 23rd academic year's joint examination for graduating middle school and physical education normal school students in this city commenced yesterday, simultaneously held in ten examination venues. Director Pan personally inspected the venues, and the order in each venue was excellent. The staff of the joint examination office worked overnight in the Lake Society, working diligently. The situation yesterday is recorded as follows:

Strict Supervision

A total of over 5,000 students participated in this joint examination and makeup examination, divided into twenty examination venues. Each venue had one chief examiner and four invigilators. Candidates from each school were accompanied to the examination venue on time by a responsible person dispatched by the school. Upon entering the venue, the admission tickets had to be checked. The seating arrangement for candidates was pre-arranged by the Education Bureau. All examination papers were sealed. The chief examiner opened them on the spot, and distributed them according to the assigned number. After the examination, the collected examination papers were still sealed by the chief examiner, with a personal seal affixed, and taken back to the Education Bureau to be reviewed and graded by the Joint Examination Committee separately. Then, the seals would be opened, and the names would be checked. The process was quite strict.

Excellent Order

Yesterday, Director Pan personally visited each examination venue to inspect and give instructions. The students in the examination venues focused on the examination papers, with vigorous spirits and excellent order. The staff of the Joint Examination Committee moved to the Lake Society to work, working overnight, quite diligently.

Today's Subjects

Today is the second day. From 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, senior and junior high school students will take mathematics. Physical education normal school students will take physiology and anatomy. From 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM, senior high school students will take geography, junior high school students will take physics and chemistry, and physical education normal school students will take history and geography. From 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM, senior high school students will take chemistry, and junior high school and physical education normal school students will take Party principles.

Education and Culture Materials of the Shen Bao Yearbook 180

Since the publication of the "1935 Shen Bao Yearbook," it has been extremely welcomed by all sectors of society. The education and culture section of the book provides a comprehensive report on the current situation of education and culture in China. It is quite beneficial for those engaged in education and students above the high school level to use it as a reference. The main contents are briefly introduced as follows:

(A) The general overview at the beginning of the education section of the book analyzes and describes in detail the important educational matters in 1934 in 39 articles. Regarding educational administration, in addition to recording the most basic and newly promulgated laws and regulations, the planning methods for special education and the resolutions of the vocational education discussion meeting are all incorporated. Statistical tables of various levels of education are added to provide reference for those engaged in education and those who want to understand the general trend of the education sector. (B) The investigation materials include the "Survey Table of National Public and Private Universities, Independent Colleges, and Vocational Schools" in January 1935, the "So-called List of Departments," and various materials on studying abroad, which are especially necessary for students preparing to go to school these days. (C) The section on rural construction and popular education experiments is well-compiled, and the general report and newly compiled statistics in the library section are comprehensive and accurate. (D) In addition to important records, the sports section contains various records approved by the National Amateur Athletic Federation at the end of 1934, and the following "Boy Scouts and National Arts" are essential for those who pay attention to sports activities. (E) The allocation tables of funds for the Sino-US, Sino-French, Sino-Belgian, and Sino-British Boxer Indemnity organizations at the end of the book are sufficient to show the relationship between the Boxer Indemnity and Chinese cultural undertakings. (F) The academic section first describes the progress of the Central and Beiping Academies, followed by the "List of National Academic Organizations," "Distribution Status Table," "Percentage Comparison Table," etc., and also contains several specialized records in the academic and cultural fields. (G) Regarding religious publications, there are many new statistics for reference. (H) The newspaper industry survey lists the national Chinese and foreign news and communication businesses in five tables, and a general situation can be seen.
