Spring and Autumn

Anecdotes 186

— (Bo Guang)

Modern young students, carrying the banner of studying as a guise, go to dance halls, watch movies, and talk about love every day, spending their parents' hard-earned money without any regret. After a few years, they get a diploma, deceiving their parents, deceiving themselves, deceiving their conscience—the black language in the academy, those who graduate from domestic universities are called "silver-plated"; those who go abroad to study are called "gold-plated"—but there are also those who study hard, but they are always a minority.

The call for promoting domestic products is deafening, but according to the customs report, there is still an excess of imported goods, which shows that the psychology of Chinese people worshiping foreign goods is too firm. A certain person produces a kind of exquisite cosmetics, and tries hard to promote it, but it is still unsalable. Later, he modified it to imitate foreign products, and it was deeply loved by modern women, and it spread like wildfire. A certain person called it "gold-plated," meaning that modern women only know how to follow blindly and do not distinguish between the quality of goods, which can be said to be a joke and abuse.

The Philosophy of Smoking Cigarettes 187

— Banana Heart

There are two people, A and B, who both have two kinds of cigarettes, one good and one bad. A offers the good ones to guests and keeps the bad ones for himself to smoke; B does the opposite, offering the bad ones to guests and keeping the good ones for himself to smoke. I was puzzled, so I went to ask A, and his answer was:

"Offering bad ones to guests is too shabby, and it will inevitably be laughed at; although it is hard for myself to eat bad ones, I will never be laughed at for being shabby, so I would rather offer good ones to guests and eat bad ones myself."

I also went to ask B, and B's reason was also very sufficient:

"Offering cigarettes to guests is a very common thing. If you offer good ones to guests, people may not necessarily thank you, so it is better to enjoy the good ones yourself."

I felt that the words of A and B both had their reasons. Later, I met Mr. C, who also had two kinds of cigarettes, but he did not necessarily offer that kind to guests, but differed according to the guest. I went to ask him what the reason was, and he said:

"I offer good cigarettes to those whose status is higher than mine, and I am not polite to those who are not as good as me and offer bad cigarettes; as for myself, I smoke good ones when I have more money, and I smoke bad ones when I have less money."

After listening to Mr. C's words, and comparing the words of A and B with each other, Mr. C's method is much more astute.

Smoking cigarettes is originally a small matter, but I didn't expect it to contain a very deep philosophy of life!

Idle Things 188

— Zhang Huang

This happened twenty years ago, just an idle thing. I was lying ill in the Ministry of Works Hospital, with a severe sore throat, fearing only death. I had no other awareness. As I gradually recovered, I was moved by a nursing girl. At that time, I was a child, only twelve years old. The girl's face and features were all [missing], I knew her to be beautiful. Her petite figure, light steps, and especially her white and clean appearance reflected in plain clothes, made people feel refreshed. I can still see it all in front of me! During her service to my illness, she was as gentle and pleasant as I wished. As we got to know each other, a few words would make me smile. I was especially impressed by her frequent visits. She called me [missing], asked about my family background, and said that she should be a matchmaker for me and find me a good wife. These were probably unintentional words, but how could I not imagine them? She spoke English wonderfully with the Western women in the hospital, like an oriole singing from a valley or a pearl rolling on a plate. I could only understand a word or two, but I was completely captivated! This [missing] girl, I think was just seventeen years old, seemed to gather the beauty of all the virgins under heaven in one body. I often thought to myself, if I could get a wife like this, what more could a husband ask for? My nephew came to visit me and asked about her illness. He praised her beauty and wisdom, and also said that she was enough to be a partner for my beloved younger brother. I silently acknowledged that he felt the same way. The girl's heart could not be guessed. I pitied my small self, insignificant and unworthy, an unequal match. In the end, I entrusted a letter [missing]—"Since the beauty left with tears, the rivers and mountains have been the ends of the earth forever. In this time when the sea and sky are yellow, I miss that beauty from afar, and can't help but feel a sense of delay?"

As I grew older, I dazzled the world with my writing, and I devoted myself to my interests, and I did not seek perfection. When my works were widely published, someone would send fresh flowers to my residence every other day, always with a small name card attached, on which the maiden name could be identified, but they soon stopped. After several months, the flowers came as before, and after another half a year, they stopped completely. Later, I accidentally learned that the person who sent the flowers was an old woman from a wealthy family. A letter of correction was found in the pile of old papers in my newly rented room. The writing was superficial, but the recipient was clearly my name. What did she give me? The intention of sending flowers with a heartfelt intention was to encourage me. From beginning to end, I felt that I was lacking in many ways, so I kept it to myself.

This is what my friend Feng Xisheng said, is it a self-description? He is now a famous writer, good at conceiving and creating novels, so it is his novel data, I don't know, I will record it for now.

Production and Armaments 189

— Tong Fu

Appreciating Music and Wonderful Words 190

— Qing Qu

The day before yesterday, I ran into an old man at Zhang's wedding banquet. He was nearly seventy years old. There were also two young men at the banquet, dressed in Western-style clothes, who were talking a lot about the Shanghai Opera tunes on their radios, which one was good and which one was bad. It really felt like they were enjoying it. The old man listened silently, holding up his wine glass and drinking non-stop. He held his chopsticks in one hand and ate with his mouth open, like raindrops. Later, the two young men also finished talking. Someone asked the old man, "Old man, do you like to listen to the radio?" The old man twirled his snow-white beard, smiled kindly, and replied, "There are several kinds of sounds that I don't like to listen to, but if I say it, I'm afraid I'll offend everyone!"

The two young men saw that he was old-fashioned and intentionally asked the old man to say it. The old man had to be impolite and said, "Alas, I'm old, not only do I not understand the radio, I don't like to listen to it. Even the most wonderful music and songs annoy me. This is my characteristic. Moreover, not only do I not like to listen to it, but I also hate listening to it very much. What are some kinds of sounds? Like the crackling sound of playing cards in the middle of the night, the sound of neighbors quarreling, and the sound of snoring when someone is still sleeping in bed when it is lunchtime. When I hear these sounds, I really want to teach them a lesson and blame them. What is the reason? Because these sounds violate the principles of life in front of us." After speaking, he pointed to the blue and white porcelain badges hanging on the two young men's clothes and asked, "What are these things?" It turned out to be the logo of implementing a new life. The two young men blushed, revealing some shame, and were nowhere to be seen.

After a while, one of the young men asked the old man angrily, "Then, old man, are there any sounds you like to listen to?" The old man said, "Yes, at home, I like to listen to my old wife opening the oil pan in the kitchen the most. It's like an eight-tone piano. Or when she puts the vegetables in the pot, it makes a crisp sound, like a thunderbolt. Isn't this an extremely good sound? Next to the river, there are several young women, using a wooden stick to pound clothes constantly. The sound of patting resonates on both sides of the river, and sometimes it wakes people up from their sweet dreams in the early morning. This kind of sound is really never tired of listening to!" When the two young men heard the old man say this, they knew that he was satirizing them, and they couldn't help but feel respectful. They bowed their hands and said, "Old man, your words are really good. After listening to these words, I can't help but remember them and present them to the readers."

Little Western Paradise 191

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: Earnest Advice and Resentment Don't Come From Nowhere, Qian Xin's Lantern Shadow is Pitifully Being Sold

At this moment, Zhiqian's blunt exposure left him speechless and blushing, head lowered. Zhiqian said, "Human compassion is something that everyone has. Your righteous indignation just now wasn't inherently wrong. However, you didn't think it through. " Beihai was even more at a loss for words. Seeing an old newspaper on the table, he casually picked it up and held it up to read. Zhiqian sat in silence for a moment, then laughed, "Actually, there's no need to worry too much. Their deal definitely won't go through. " Beihai asked, "What's the reason for that?" Zhiqian said, "They, three generations of them – two widows and a girl – escaped from Gansu to this place. They've already made it this far. How could they possibly separate and sell family members in a place where they can beg for food?" Beihai said, "I think so too. But if this deal doesn't go through, that Hu Xiaoming family won't keep them living there anymore. Where will they go to settle down then?" As he said this, he was genuinely worried for them. He put down the newspaper, put his hands behind his back, and paced back and forth in the room. Zhiqian didn't stop him, letting him worry as he pleased. While he was pacing, he caught sight of Yang Huanhua hurrying past the window. It was clear that she had already gotten a result at the Hu Xiaoming's house and was going to report to Jia Duocai. So, this matter was a success. He suddenly turned around, ready to walk out the door. But at the same time, he saw Zhiqian smiling slightly at the side, and he immediately suppressed his impulse to rush out. Zhiqian smiled, "That Miss Yang just passed by the window. You could go ask Zhong and inquire about some news. " Zhiqian's bluntness made him blush even more, looking embarrassed. He forced a smile and said, "Their affairs aren't worth my attention." (248)

Records of Fragrant Mists 192

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

After she finished speaking that passage, I couldn't help but feel secretly doubtful again, wondering if the Empress Dowager herself truly believed in the so-called "mischievous creator": but I dared not ask her rashly, because I still remembered the reprimand I received in Fengtian for the Green Fox Immortal incident. But the Empress Dowager's eyesight was truly sharp, and she had already seen the doubts lurking in my heart, so without waiting for me to ask, she added another explanation for me.

"We certainly cannot guarantee that there truly is such a deity in the world, we can only say that perhaps there is; but there are many such divine beings that we cannot see with our own eyes, and their existence is often undeniable to us. You might as well try to think about it: in your past experiences, have you ever had the experience of everything going extremely smoothly, especially, and then suddenly various unexpected problems arise, making you feel extremely frustrated; I think this is absolutely unavoidable! And the one who frustrates you in the dark is the so-called 'mischievous creator'!"

As soon as she said this, I knew that she herself had at least half a belief in this mischievous creator who was neither an immortal nor a Buddha. I couldn't help but feel very happy, deeply pleased that I had not dared to make reckless criticisms just now, otherwise I would have suffered another scolding. Because the old woman had this kind of belief in her heart, it made her feel uneasy all the time: for example, after she had played a little more happily today, she was worried that something unfortunate would happen, or even had the fear that if it didn't happen today, it would definitely happen tomorrow. (248)

Global Rare News

Japanese Chinese Cuisine 193

— Jiyun

Overseas Chinese in Japan are mostly in Yokohama and Tokyo. They either open grocery stores or Chinese restaurants and tea houses. Other businesses are difficult to compete with the Japanese, so they are rarely seen. The Japanese call cuisine "ryori," and Chinese restaurants are called "Chuka ryori" (Chinese cuisine). These overseas Chinese are mostly from Beijing, Shandong, Ningbo, Guangdong, and other places, especially Ningbo. In various districts of Tokyo, there is nowhere without their businesses. Even though they are all Chinese cuisines, the seasoning methods are also different. Northern restaurants mostly sell steamed buns and mantou. The seasoning also removes the spicy smell of scallions and garlic. Southern restaurants emphasize assorted dishes. Chinese noodles and shumai are famous.

Japanese people who have eaten Chinese cuisine have no choice but to praise the excellence of the Chinese people's seasoning methods. Even laborers who eat bento (lunch boxes) every day often ask friends to try Chinese noodles once. Chinese and Japanese newspapers and magazines also often have seasoning guides for Chinese cuisine. However, most of them are seasoning methods for Chinese restaurants, which are not suitable for home cooking, and not many Japanese people are trying to imitate them. The so-called Chinese noodles are just ordinary Chinese soup noodles. On top are a few slices of meat as thin as ham and a few Taiwan bamboo shoots. The price is about ten cents, and the profit is not small. Shumai are different from those in our country. They are balls made of minced meat and cabbage, wrapped in flour and made into a round shape. Because there is very little minced meat, the cost is light, so four or five can be bought for ten cents.

Japanese people have learned the rudiments of our country's seasoning methods and are also competing with the stores, hanging up Chinese cuisine signs. Moreover, there is also a Shaoxing wine jar at the door, with colorful pictures on it, indicating a sign that they can't cook Chinese dishes. These empty wine jars are sold in secondhand stores for as much as one yuan and eighty cents each. Chinese restaurants all sell wine imported from China, such as Wujiapi, Shaoxing wine, and yellow wine. Each jar has customs duties of four or five yuan or more, so the price is very expensive. Moreover, the taste of the wine is stronger than Japanese wine, so not many people come to try it. In addition, there are pumpkin seeds, watermelon seeds, large green plums, and preserved eggs on display in the display cabinet, plus tin-made hot pots and longevity candle stands. Who would think that they are living in a foreign country?

In the Kanda district, where there are the most foreign students, Chinese food sells even more. The store is full of Chinese students, and some people can't find a seat and leave. Because of different provinces and dialects, Chinese people can only speak to each other in Japanese, which is what we feel is the most difficult thing. But the Japanese language is not unified either. People from Tokyo and Nagasaki need an interpreter to talk to each other.

Foreign students have a special kind of packed lunch called "teishoku" (set meal), which costs about twenty cents per meal. Although the dish and soup are simple, they are much better than the raw and cold Japanese dishes. Not being able to eat large pieces of meat in Japan is a serious problem. Japanese people like to eat vegetables and fish, so there are not many butcher shops and the prices are also very expensive. I heard that Japanese people slaughter pigs in an unconventional way: they beat the pigs to death with sticks, and then skin them, like killing cows. So there is indeed no skin on the pork. Also, the kidneys and feet, which are considered precious in our country, are not eaten by them. So Chinese restaurants have a lot of cheap goods. Four pig's feet can be obtained for ten cents, so the twenty-cent set meal can also include one pig's foot.

A full course of dishes costs about eight yuan to more or less. Apart from Chinese banquets, Japanese people don't often ask people to eat them. One reason is that the price is too expensive, and the second is that Japanese people eat separately. Many people sitting around eating together is not customary.

Free Talk

On Gogol's Descriptive Method 210

— Qu Yi

After reading Mr. Ding Jun's "On Gogol's Method of Describing Characters" from the "Zishan Tan" on the 22nd, I felt the same way. Indeed, Gogol's "novelistic approach" when introducing characters can significantly impact the integrity and unity of a work. However, strangely, when we read "The Overcoat," "The Nose," and "Dead Souls," we don't feel that his work is fragmented because of it. Instead, we feel it increases the broader social atmosphere of his characters. This is indeed worth pondering deeply.

Originally, in old realist literature, this style of describing characters for a while, or when the characters are brought into the scene, with the author personally stepping forward to speak, was very common. For example, "Dream of the Red Chamber" begins by saying, "This is the first chapter of the book," and then explains the reasons for the book's creation at length. Similarly, in "The Ingenious Hidalgo Don Quixote of La Mancha" and the first chapter of "The True Story of Ah Q," there is a whole series of idle talks that are both true and false. The author is like a storyteller, sitting on a high stool leaning against a table, striking the gavel, and rambling on, with that attitude and demeanor. Sometimes, as in old Chinese vernacular novels, halfway through the story, there's a bit like, "Look, officials, what, what," kind of idle talk. — Those idle talks are mostly the author's feelings or arguments — In my opinion, these parts often use the characteristics of old realism: the so-called flat development of the story, and the static unfolding of the scene, to provide answers. And these characteristics and techniques of old realism seem to be traceable to all kinds of novels and romances, from oral transmission and narration in feudal society, to being moved onto books when the printing industry developed. So no matter how much it tries to break away from the storyteller's attitude, it engages in writing. Once novelists gradually moved away from that era of oral performance (although storytellers still exist in society, such as Chinese storytellers with drums), literary works gradually became non-popular reading materials, and the seriousness of the work gradually increased.

The appearance of characters and the unfolding of scenes in the work are driven by the work itself, and the author is completely hidden behind the book, without revealing any trace of their face. This technique easily captures the reader, allowing them to blend into the work and share the characters' sorrows and joys. This is a common example in the history of literary evolution, both in China and abroad. In Gogol's works, the interjections where he comes forward himself also have this factor involved. But those interjections, and his work are so harmonious and integrated, which relates to his style.

Speaking of Gogol's works that I have read: such as "The Government Inspector," "The Overcoat," and "The Nose," they can mostly be said to belong to the category of satirical literature. But his satirical literature is different from other satirical literature. General satirical literature authors are good at decorating their words with sharp needles, and their appearance is blatant; it is easy for the object of satire to get hurt in their flesh. Gogol's satire, however, combines the work itself with the satirical purpose. The entire work is a sword and a knife, a rifle and a dagger. For example, take "The Nose"! Finding a nose in a loaf of bread, a Collegiate Assessor finds his nose sitting in a carriage as a State Councillor. Or take "The Government Inspector," receiving a Government Inspector and ending up receiving a traveler in the hotel, and even giving away his own daughter in the process. Judging by the story, it can be said to be extremely absurd. It can be said to be extremely unreasonable. However, through this absurd story, through this unreasonable description, the reader sees an extremely real side. And finally, a cold dagger is deeply planted in the reader's heart; making the reader unable to resist, and both laugh and cry. Gogol's authorship has been so popular with readers to this day, and this is where his reason lies. Because truth is the life of all literature. In Gogol's works, we see the living dead souls of the declining landlord class (as depicted in his "Old-World Landowners") and the rotten aristocratic class.

However, in fact, Gogol himself belonged to the aristocratic landlord class. Although he hated the characters in his own class very much, he couldn't get rid of the essential atmosphere of this class. (For example, in "Old-World Landowners," he describes Afanasy Ivanovich and Pulkheria Ivanovna's death entirely with a very sympathetic and compassionate attitude.) And when he wanted to describe these hateful characters, he had to use oblique strokes to avoid factual troubles. Therefore, he created extremely absurd stories to cover up the true face of reality. (In fact, the true face of reality shines through even more because of his clever cover-up.) Since the story is so absurd, then in the development of the writing style, he had to use extraordinary methods; he deliberately disguised himself as a clown, smearing a strip of white powder on his nose, and telling a set of sad jokes. So when we talk about "The Overcoat" and "Dead Souls," even though he inserts large paragraphs of idle talk from time to time, we still feel that the work is integrated, unified, and complete. That is because his extraordinary techniques – form – and the absurd story – content – are very consistent.

In today's China, it seems that there is a great need for authors who can use methods like Gogol's, because the reality we are facing is a very difficult era. I wrote this short essay, although the motive was to answer Mr. Gu Dingjun's inconclusive thinking, but the meaning is to tell Chinese realist writers, when you can't write, learn Gogol's cleverness!

I Also Want to Talk About Sanitary Stinky Tofu 211

— Chen Zizhan

Old Man Zhitang is dissatisfied with the scientific essays commonly seen in current various Mao publications, and he compares these essays to sanitary stinky tofu. Naturally. Some essays are like stinky tofu. But it is not necessarily the case with scientific essays. Speaking of stinky tofu, it seems to be popular everywhere, but I always feel that only the ones from Changsha are good. I dare to swear that I am not promoting it, especially since I only occasionally buy it to taste, and I have never eaten it as a meal. Changsha's fried tofu may not be particularly wonderful, but it just suits my taste, and that's good enough. As for hygiene, I consider it secondary. Old Man Zhitang also loves to eat stinky tofu. And he only says that the ones from the Gongan and Jingling families are good, each to their own taste, please feel free to choose. But he always wants to introduce the goods from the Gongan and Jingling families to everyone, like a candy seller saying the candy is sweet, and a wine seller saying the wine is good, writing a special book as an advertisement. Then he would inevitably commit the suspicion of promoting sanitary stinky tofu.

Also, Old Man Zhitang believes in fate. He says: "Recently I have come to believe in fate a bit. So, should I go to consult a certain master or astrologer, and ask him to point out the good and bad luck of my fleeting years or my whole life? That is not necessarily the case. I can know these things myself. Because no one knows oneself better than oneself. I believe in fate, not based on my family's Book of Changes divine divination, but on other people's scientific numerology. When I say fate, I mean the individual's innate qualities, now called heredity. When I say luck, I mean the acquired influences, now called environment." — The theory of fate has always been just stinky tofu, even Old Man Zhitang, who is so wise and intelligent, doesn't he know this? If he wants to believe in the theory of fate, he has to make Western-style improvements, especially in hygiene. He distorts the theories of heredity and environment of Western biologists, and turns them into his new theory of fate. He advocates the new theory of fate based on "scientific numerology." This is also like a stinky tofu seller advertising "hygiene." What I think can be likened to sanitary stinky tofu is the so-called "scientific numerology of fate" and "scientific spirit mediumship." But this is not necessarily the same as a scientific essay.

Summer in the Mountain City 212

— Shen Shengshi

Surrounded by mountains on three sides. The fiery tongues of the sun lick down from the mountain peaks. Scorching the fresh green grass on the mountainside, and even licking the pools of water at the foot of the mountain dry.

The streets of the mountain city. Like in a big, scalding steamer now.

Originally a place without water, the water problem is even more pressing now.

The Daquan well in Siyan Cave at the foot of the mountain runs out of water by noon, but the water carriers with their water carts and buckets still come in batches, scrambling to hoist up the water. The large wooden buckets sway in the deep, seemingly bottomless well, and after swaying for a long time, only half a bucket of yellow mud water is hoisted up. People are still fighting for the yellow mud water.

The riverbed of the Huai River is exposed layer by layer in the sunlight. The water carriers who go to fetch water have to walk down the tiers of banks, and when they reach the water, there is only a thin layer of water, and the large wooden buckets cannot scoop it up. Of course, there is still a lot of water in the center of the riverbed, but the wind and waves are strong, and people cannot stand still when they go into the water; so people are digging holes along the Huai River, and more than a dozen large buckets are taking turns scooping buckets of yellow mud water from the newly dug water holes.

Going up the mountain for tea, the old Taoist priest tells us that the mountain spring has dried up: we see a child scooping mud water with a small spoon in a deep stone depression. After scooping for a long time, he cannot scoop up even half a spoon. The mud water can't be scooped up either.

Everyone is unanimously hoping for rain. It rained a few days ago, but the rain was not heavy enough to make a difference, and only muddy water is still being hoisted up from the well.

Summer in the mountain city is truly unbearable to live in any longer; walking up the street at dusk, the street is filled with a pungent, acrid odor.

Bare-bodied, stark naked children run back and forth in groups, their dirty black bodies covered in rust-like patterns, perhaps they haven't taken a bath in a year or so!

At night, the old and the young lie out in the streets, sleeping in the open air; their bare bodies are displayed in the moonlight.

From seeing teams of mud water buckets on the street during the day, to the exhibition of bare bodies in the streets at night, this place will make you not dare to stay any longer.

University Days (10) 213

— By German writer, Theodor Storm, translated by Chen Yin Zhi

But Nana wasn't in the hall anymore, the other girls were standing next to their mothers, their mothers were tidying up their straps and ribbons. Mrs. Bolica was bringing in refreshments; she didn't see her daughter either. Now I went to look for Fritz, who was standing next to the music stand in the corner of the room, filling up the empty cups. "Where's Nana?" I asked.

"I don't know," he replied with a displeased face, "She was silent as a dumb man just now, I don't know why."

I pulled him out into the hallway; as we walked past the room where the guests' coats were placed, we ran into her; she had already put on her coat and wrapped the black silk scarf around her head. "Nali!" I shouted, trying to grab her hand, but she broke free of her hand and walked past us.

"Don't nag!" she said simply, "I'm going home!"

A moment later, she forcefully pulled open the heavy door leading to the street and ran out, jumping and skipping, walking down the steps next to the lamp post. When Fritz followed her to the door, she had already walked far away on the street, and we could only see her running figure in the dark.

"Let her go!" Fritz said, "Are you interested in chasing wild geese?"

I did have this interest: but I didn't know if I should do this. — We had to go back to the hall. Mrs. Bolica went home to take care of something, but came back again before she was finished, — saying that Nali was feeling unwell and was already asleep in bed, her mother's father was sitting next to her.

I felt uncomfortable all night: just as the "Gottingen Dance" that I wanted to dance with Nana was about to begin, I quietly and sullenly went home.

Job Application 215

— Li Huiying

Luo Fei walked into the manager's office of a certain company, she was here to apply for a job. The manager asked her:

"Are you called Luo Fei?"

"Yes."

"Ah, Miss Luo, Miss Luo, how old are you?"

"Twenty-three years old."

The manager took out the photo that Luo Fei had sent when she applied and compared it, as if scrutinizing whether the face of the person who came was the same as the photo. This manager of a certain company was short and fat, wearing a neat Western suit, his shirt as white as if it had been brushed with a layer of powder, his hair shiny with oil, so that flies would fall over if they landed on it, his face fleshy and tender, one could imagine that he used cold cream and perfume every year, his eyes were like shooting stars, his mustache was shaped like the Chinese character "eight," and his lips were cracked open, as if deliberately asking him to smile at others more. Yes, the manager was smiling. He continued:

"Miss Luo, your ancestral home is Suzhou, ah."

In fact, Luo Fei's age, hometown, and resume were all clearly written on the application letter, asking or not asking, it was all the same routine.

"Yes."

"Ah, Suzhou, I just remembered, Suzhou produces beauties, ah." He stroked his mustache. "No wonder Miss Luo, hahaha, you are so beautiful. Indeed, the reputation is well-deserved." Saying this, he changed the topic and pretended to be very serious, asking: "How well do you type, Miss Luo?"

Luo Fei nodded. She didn't know how to reply. She just felt that the manager's eyes were like two arrows, aiming at her, ready to be shot, his words were also very frivolous, she was anxious in her heart, and her face turned red for a while.

"Are you shy? Really good, really beautiful."

The manager leaned his head further, staring at her tightly, looking her up and down, and then asked: "Are you married?"

"Me?——Later," "I'm not engaged yet."

"Then you are a real Miss, haha, great, great."

Luo Fei was extremely embarrassed, and truly felt that it was the first time in her life that she had been ridiculed by others, and she never let people get away with it, but now, in order to find a job, she had no choice but to endure and not argue with others about these things. Luo Fei wanted to stand up and run out of the manager's office, find Lu Wen, — her husband — who was waiting for her at the pier on the riverbank, and hug him and cry. She was angry, unable to restrain herself, and said seriously:

"Mr. Manager, would you please say less about irrelevant matters?"

"Irrelevant matters? Haha." He stretched out his hand and stroked his oily hair again. "You can't say that, I mean to test whether you are generous — What are you busy with, isn't it good to sit for a while longer? I think you are very good, ah, yes, you are very good, you type and see."

Luo Fei walked to the typewriter and sat down, stretched out her hand, ready to listen to the manager's instructions.

"I'll say it, you follow along and type, okay?"

Luo Fei nodded in agreement.

"Ah, great, I'll say it, listen, it's starting. — Friend, why didn't you come yesterday? It doesn't matter if you didn't come, it's not right to make me wait for a long time. Ah, I remember, you were probably entangled by that Miss, right? That Miss of yours is indeed charming, if I were you, I would inevitably be entangled by her and unable to get away, am I right? — Finished."

Luo Fei's hands stopped following along.

"Very fast, very fast, great."

After Luo Fei handed over the paper, she thought to herself: Is this what the female staff in the company do? She couldn't help but laugh to herself.

"You type very well, not a single word is wrong, you are very good." The manager said gleefully. "I'll ask you again, Miss Luo, are you married after all?"

"Not at all!" Luo Fei said very decisively. "But, why do you keep asking me this? Is it relevant?"

"Ah, it's relevant, of course it is, unmarried people are meticulous in their work, and……" (To be continued)

Storm 216

— Ouyang Fan Hai

A dark and vast world… That

Beneath the sky, above the ground,

The roar of a storm surges!

Angry thunder whips the Earth,

Lightning lifts its head from wickedness, tearing at flames like ripped silk!

I raise my head, reaching out the window,

Staring with burning eyes,

Vying to glimpse a trace of lightning,

Yet unable to see through this boundless, desolate smoke of hate and raging waves,

I only see racing clouds engulfing the horizon, drawing closer and closer,

Like a dark, pressing mass of creatures,

About to rush into that moment of life and death—

Once, a thin white line of the human world in the sky,

Gradually mixing into a mass of blackness;

The storm and lightning seem to hate not being able to crush the Earth's crust,

Shaking and scattering, unable to see anything anymore!

I know that crackling thunderclap,

Is brewing a fatal blow in the unseen blackness!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

On Suicide Due to Unrequited Love 217

— Tie Sheng

This month, I saw the news about Wang Shouchang, a student at the Law School, committing suicide due to unrequited love in the local news column. After reading it, I felt a sense of loss for a long time, and a sense of sadness lingered deeply in my mind. Recently, due to the rapid collapse of the national economy and the desperate situation of the national life, the epidemic of suicide is spreading like the plague at an accelerating rate. The suicide of Wang Shouchang, a university student, is a unique case. As an excellent young man who has received a university education, when the country and society rely on him the most, he suddenly commits suicide due to unrequited love. It is truly pitiful, and laughably foolish! Almost everyone who hears about it scolds him for "not being worth such a sacrifice!"

We know that in this deformed capitalist society, when everything has become a commodity, the bewitching term "love" has also taken on the stench of copper and become commodified. Wealthy merchants and magnates can certainly take it inexhaustibly and enjoy it at will; however, for a poor person who is as poor as a church mouse to want the gift of love, it is truly like a toad wanting to eat swan meat. In this deformed society, "love" has become a deformed existence and a perverted development. "So-called love is mystical," and "love transcends everything," only children who do not understand the ways of the world have such fantasies. In this deformed society, we hope that love will restore its original true face — to be reasonably and satisfactorily resolved by everyone. That can only happen after this unreasonable economic system is thoroughly changed.

We also know that love is not the entirety of life, but merely an optional embellishment on the journey of life. It is good to have it, but it is the same to survive without it. Or it may even reduce the burden of life. We see many people starving to death because they have no food to eat, but we have not seen anyone die immediately because they have no love. Moreover, the mission that the present era has given to us young people is absolutely important. It is permissible for us to sacrifice love for the sake of the mission of the era; but it is absolutely impermissible for us to sacrifice the mission given to us by the era for the sake of love. As the saying goes: "Death can be heavier than Mount Tai, or lighter than a feather." Does Wang Shouchang's suicide due to unrequited love this time give people even a trace of sympathy? As for those who are forced to commit suicide due to the pressure of life, there is still room for pity, however, this is definitely not the correct way out of life. The way out of life is consistent with the way out of society. Only by facing reality, striving through hardship, and overcoming difficulties can one find the true way out of life. I think that if Wang Shouchang had a correct understanding, he would never have made this meaningless sacrifice. May the young men and women who are trapped in the battlefield of love beware of wasting their lives again!

Sishui Night Market 218

— Lini

Living every day under the scorching sun of the southern country, amidst the bustling atmosphere of traffic and commerce, my frail body and mind have indeed grown a bit weary of the city's prosperity and liveliness. Therefore, the street's hustle and bustle, and the various potent temptations of the amusement parks, even the unique, beautiful, comfortable, and cool nights of the south, can't stir my mood to join the revelry. Nor can they entice me to take a full flask of wine to a quiet and tranquil place, sitting beneath the lush, umbrella-like trees, harmonizing with the silver-bell-like murmuring streams, leisurely playing music. Instead, I always prefer to be listlessly confined in my desolate room, facing the solitary lamp, quietly resting my exhausted spirit. Sometimes, I close my eyes and indulge in foolish reveries, dreaming happy dreams.

But tonight is a bit different. The crackling sound of firecrackers, music, dragon lanterns, costume parades... noisily parade around the entire town. People are packed as tightly as ants, chest to back, back to chest, filling the streets and alleys in rows. This can't help but stir the tranquil sea of my heart. The once-a-year night market, seemingly specially set up for the New Year, has officially opened.

The duration of the night market, as usual, starts three days before New Year's Eve and lasts until New Year's Eve. However, most merchants, for the sake of commercial prosperity, habitually extend it until after the Lantern Festival before ending the night market. The location of the night market originally has a designated place, but those places don't have permanent buildings. Therefore, when the night market is held, temporary bamboo sheds are set up, equipped with bright electric lights, and rented out to various merchants from near and far, displaying and selling all kinds of goods, creating this once-a-year, exceptionally lively night market.

The desolate and quiet room seems to have lost its magic, making my heart yearn for the spring. After taking a cold shower after dinner, I no longer went into the room, squeezed into the layers of the crowd, smelling the strong, turbid, and sweat-sour odor that made my nostrils uncomfortable, and the pungent stimulating scent of betel nuts, and was pushed by the human tide into the market.

The night market is simply an amusement park. Inside, besides people squeezing people and people watching people, there are also those colorful daily necessities and various novelties, such as: leather monkey shows, song and dance troupes, strongmen, airplanes, wooden horses, Ferris wheels, etc. These are all things that I have grown tired of visiting in amusement parks in various cities, and they no longer stir my heartstrings, which made me pay attention to. What can most arouse my attention are those exhibition halls. Their layout, decoration, and explanation can all make me feel satisfied and leave a deep impression. For example, some factories not only display their products but also bring their heavy machinery, and at the same time, actually manufacture goods, so that visitors can know the manufacturing process of a certain product, and express their seriousness in manufacturing, and have a deep impression of a certain commodity.

When I stepped into the exhibition hall of the Health Bureau, suddenly, I deeply felt that their promotion of public health was truly meticulous! What is displayed this year is the dental department. In addition to the associated display of various animal teeth, human teeth, whether they are overlapping teeth, piercing teeth, double teeth, or various forms of teeth with arrangement variations, are all truly unseen and collected exhaustively. At the same time, various facial deformities of patients with various dental diseases are hung on the walls, making people feel frightened at first glance, and their whole body can't help but break out in goosebumps. Turning into the inner room, various models of decayed teeth are displayed inside. Incisors, molars, canines, middle cavities, side cavities, etc., all have quite conspicuous large models. Finally, a microscope is displayed, placing specially made bacterial cultures of decayed teeth on a glass slide under the microscope, allowing visitors to clearly recognize their shape through the microscope. At the exit, many posters reminding people to brush their teeth, as well as photos of clean and beautiful teeth after brushing, are hung. Such education is integrated into entertainment, and the broad effect is far better than in the classroom. This cannot but make me admire the excellent methods of promotion by their executives!

Depression and Loneliness 219

— Shi Weizhi

In the past, I could only see the words "depression" and "loneliness" in books. At that time, the burden of life had not yet been shouldered. To shout, "depression" and "loneliness," was originally the same as shouting about spring flowers and autumn moons, a kind of pretense to decorate oneself. Leaning in the arms of a lover, seeing the withered flowers and waning moon, then coquettishly: "Life is depressing!" "Life is lonely!"

Not long afterward, stepping from school into the steps of society, I then knew what "depression" and "loneliness" actually were. Seeing my friends gradually aging before these two terms, gradually falling down, I couldn't help but feel a shadow in my heart, feeling that I had also been crawled into my chest by the germs of "depression" and "loneliness." Later, I myself shouldered the burden of life. Moreover, I hit a wall, and my youthful aspirations disappeared in a forced struggle. I no longer had any ambition. I only wanted to make my burden of life more stable, so that it would not collide with others, so as not to add unexpected weight to my burden, so as not to be crushed because of the increased unexpected weight.

Towards my career, I lost my ambition. Towards home, I was a little afraid—home had never given me the slightest benefit! In this way, I knew that my chest not only had "depression" and "loneliness," but was also occupied by "depression" and "loneliness."

I felt more and more lonely, even to the point where I realized that once I fell dead by the roadside, I would only have four pine boards to sleep on. - Giving me pine boards to sleep on is not the kindness of philanthropists. On the contrary, this is their "business," and at the same time, they are afraid that this dead person will bring them the epidemic.

This spring, when the "depression" grew more and more intense, as Hu Kao said, I got a chance to go to Hangzhou. Therefore, half to fulfill a long-cherished wish, and half to treat my "depression," I scraped together a few dollars with great difficulty, mixed in with the ranks of young masters and young ladies, and started my "spring trip."

In Hangzhou, I clearly realized that "depression" and "loneliness" originally had some differences.

That is to say, after arriving in Hangzhou, depression was temporarily forgotten, but what followed was "loneliness."

However, there were many more lonely people. When, on a windy and rainy evening in a hotel, a singing girl who was past her prime desperately shouted with her hoarse voice, I quietly closed the door and cried. Naturally, in the song, I heard her anger.

After a week, I took my slender shadow, and also took "depression" and "loneliness," and still returned to Shanghai. The spring trip did not cure my "depression" and "loneliness."

In order to get rid of "depression" and "loneliness," I began to seek stimulation, to seek stimulation as much as possible. Using alcohol, using dancing, using all meaningless and boring actions to temporarily numb my nerves.

However, I couldn't. All the stimulation was not enough to numb me. On the contrary, all the stimulation made me even more painful. The wound of "depression" did not heal, and I discovered more souls of "loneliness."

Now, I don't want to seek stimulation anymore. I only want to enjoy loneliness quietly, letting my soul glue to the silken threads of loneliness. This world is lonely, and in loneliness, I should learn something.

When the hell of loneliness is broken, or perhaps the shackles of "depression" can also be removed.

But when will the hell of loneliness be broken? Friend!

It's okay to have no companion, just step forward on the journey alone. Isn't that long shadow illuminated by the moonlight your best companion?

Drag your slender shadow, sing your song of loneliness with your hoarse voice. Human life is lonely, but there are many who feel the loneliness of human life.

Saltwater Girl 220

— Hu Kao

The Oil Shop (Part Two) 221

— Ruizhi

His heart was conflicted; his thoughts all day long revolved around this point, but after racking his brains to think, he still couldn't find a solution, sometimes to the point of a headache.

He was over fifty years old this year. Although he had four sons, one had died, and another had gone missing at the age of fifteen. Now, only two remained. In the years when business was still good, he always thought of his eldest son, who had gone missing. He thought, "If he comes back, this business can be handed over to him." But now? He was still thinking, but his thoughts were different from before. He didn't want him to come back to manage the business, but hoped that his son would suddenly make a fortune and return.

He often said to the two sons living at home: "Although your eldest brother doesn't do proper work, he is very smart. After being outside for more than ten years, if he is still alive, he will definitely make a fortune. The fortune teller said when he was young that he would definitely make a fortune after he turned thirty. Now he is over thirty, so he will definitely come back."

Old Zhou had been saying these words to his two sons for several years, but he was always waiting, but he didn't see his son who was going to make a fortune return.

The depression in the town was getting worse and worse. Shops were closing down on the street every day, which made it impossible for Old Zhou to continue to support himself. But he still wanted to struggle; he didn't want to see this ancestral shop closed with those dilapidated door panels in his hands. He tried every method, but everything was useless. The most important fact was that no one came to trade. Although there was no income, expenses were unavoidable. In the end, he sent his two remaining sons to other places to seek their own livelihood. Only he and his old wife were left. The oil shop was still open as usual, but for a long thirty days, there were only a few customers. Spiders were weaving webs on those oil tanks.

Page 19

The History of Piłsudski's Struggle (Part Two) 222

— Nan

The General deeply understood that Poland was surrounded by strong neighbors coveting its land. To maintain domestic and international peace and avoid invasion by enemy countries, it was necessary to train the strongest possible army to resist foreign aggression at any time. Therefore, he devoted himself to training the army, and its strength grew day by day. In 1920, the Russian Red Army pressed on the border, threatening the newly liberated Poland. After several bitter battles, the Russian Red Army was as unstoppable as a broken bamboo, directly approaching Warsaw, only eight miles from the city. At this time, the General used his intelligence and bravery to lead the newly trained army in a fierce counterattack. After two weeks of fierce fighting, he completely defeated the enemy. He safeguarded the peace of Poland and all of Europe. His achievements were most remarkable. At that time, Poland's situation was indeed extremely critical, and all countries believed that Poland's life had been extinguished. When the victory spread, the world was shocked, because the disparity between the strong and the weak was so great that there was no chance of victory unless the officers and soldiers all embraced the determination to die. The reputation of the Polish army soared. In this battle, the General captured 115,000 Red Army soldiers, 390 cannons, 7 armored vehicles, 2,000 machine guns, and 1,000 freight cars of military supplies and industrial materials, and 2,600 trains. The Red Army's four combat armies, the 111th Army, were completely annihilated, and the remaining two armies suffered extremely heavy losses. After the war, the General actively focused on domestic construction, improving the political, economic, social, and cultural situation, and integrating the opinions of various political parties to concentrate forces and revive the country.

The General was not a dictator, but a great educator. However, overseas countries regarded him as a dictator. In fact, this term was not carefully chosen. The term dictator can be applied to Mussolini, Hitler, and Kemal, but the General should be regarded as "The Deciding Factor" in Poland, which is more realistic. The General's foreign policy was the same as his domestic policy, aimed at giving Poland the opportunity to develop and achieve peace. In other words, the foreign policy was a policy of land neighbors, making Poland friendly with its two strong neighbors, Russia and Germany, and signing non-aggression treaties.

The General sacrificed himself for his country throughout his life. First, for the independence of the country, and second, for the great development and promotion of the country's future. Before his death, the General was able to see Poland become stronger and respected by various countries, and the continuous efforts of the entire country, both government and public, to steadily overcome the difficulties of the world economic recession and currency wars, and move forward to a bright future, which was truly a very fortunate thing. The General has now completed his work, which the Polish people have been unable to do for thousands of years. The General is dead, but the memories of his teachings, deeds, and achievements, and his spirit of endless struggle, will never diminish. The General is not only a leader, but also a modern liberator, educator, and builder of Poland. The General is Poland, and he will forever reside in the hearts of the Polish people, and will exist forever with the Polish nation. (The End)

Amateur Mailbox

Procedures for Withdrawing from a Joint Venture Shop 223

Editor:

Three years ago, I partnered with friends to start a cotton yarn company. The capital was a total of 12,000 yuan, and I invested 3,000 yuan. The store is managed by the major shareholder, Mr. Wang, who handles everything. At first, business was not bad, but in the past year or two, due to the impact of the economic panic and the current situation, it has gradually been losing money. Considering my weak financial resources, I am deeply afraid that if I continue vaguely, I will lose a large sum in the future. Not only will my years of hard work be in vain, but I may also be responsible for liquidation at that time, which I will not be able to afford. Therefore, I contacted the manager, Mr. Wang, and requested to withdraw and take back the remaining capital. However, Mr. Wang refused, based on some unknown point, which really puzzled me. I don't know if my request is unreasonable. Please give me an indication. Thank you in advance.

Sincerely, Zhang Wengeng

Editor's note: Failure is the mother of success. Setbacks before the success of a great undertaking are inevitable. Therefore, we feel that if Mr. Zhang has strong financial resources and believes that the company has the hope of development, then we should advise him not to be discouraged and continue to do so. As long as he can continue to work hard, the future can be optimistic. However, according to the letter, Mr. Zhang's financial resources do not seem to be very strong. Then, for the sake of prudence, it is certainly right to want to break away from the relationship and reduce the risk.

The cotton yarn company is a partnership business. Each shareholder bears full and unlimited liability for the profits and losses of the store. If it continues vaguely, the responsibility is very heavy. Therefore, the law stipulates that after the annual accounts are settled, shareholders have the right to apply for withdrawal. Mr. Zhang can argue on the basis of reason and negotiate with Mr. Wang. If a compromise can be reached, it must still be declared in the newspaper truthfully. Otherwise, Mr. Zhang and Mr. Wang's non-public procedures cannot resist "unknowing third parties" in law, and disputes cannot be avoided. In the event that Mr. Wang insists on not allowing it, Mr. Zhang can declare in the newspaper that he has separated from the company since a certain time, and at the same time, submit it to the court for record. As for the negotiation of recovering the remaining capital, it should be carried out in another case.

About Nora 228

Ibsen's dramas depict each character's life very vividly. Take the play Nora, for example. His narrative of the personalities of the five main characters is lively and vivid. He writes about the contradictions of human nature, good and evil, and the entanglement of love between men and women. He gives an answer in the midst of not finding an answer. This amateur theater group's first joint performance is performed by five of the most skilled stage actors. Each actor can understand the characters that Ibsen wanted to write.

The overall stage performance has a beautiful and tranquil taste. It is a story from 19th-century Northern Europe, so it has the style of the film "Grievance of a Young Woman." Furthermore, it narrates the situation of celebrating Christmas, so it also has the beautiful sentiment of Andersen's "The Little Match Girl." The snow scene outside a large window in the set is simply a portrayal of that fairy tale.

Hollywood Silver Wave United Artists Company's Plans After Reform 230

United Artists Company was originally organized by the four giants "Pickford, Chaplin, Fairbanks, and San Gawen." Recently, due to the departure of its former general manager and the appointment of a new one, its internal structure has been greatly reformed. In addition to the original producers, David O. Selznick, the current MGM supervisor, has been hired as the general supervisor. James is truly one of the leading producers. His famous works include "A Tale of Two Cities," "Dinner at Eight," and "Viva Villa!" After joining United Artists, James will produce six films each year.

Chaplin has been absent for four years since he met the audience in "City Lights." His new film will be released soon, and it is expected to be released this fall. The title has not yet been decided, and it is temporarily named "Production No. 5." According to Chaplin himself, the content is quite simple, depicting the lives of two workers. Although this film has music, it still has no dialogue. After this work, Chaplin plans to direct a film with Goddard as the female lead.

In United Artists Company's 1936 productions, in addition to the aforementioned Chaplin's new work, the films produced by Corwin and starring Edith Contay and Anna Sten are also excellent. Other productions such as those by King Vidor and the London Company are still distributed by United Artists.

Shenbao Architecture Weekly

The Process of Architecture and Architectural Materials in This City (1) 233

— Gu Ying

Timber imports in the first four months of this year increased by four million compared to the same period last year. Since the implementation of the new tax, cement imports are only one-fifth of what they were three years ago.

Living and transportation are essential elements of life. Therefore, the expansion of the population and the progress of the construction industry go hand in hand. In recent years, the construction industry has also advanced with the population. Unfortunately, building materials such as timber, cement, and steel are mostly imported goods, and Chinese people are happy to use them. Therefore, the import of foreign timber and other materials increases year by year. Since the increase in tariffs on cement and the implementation of the new tax, imports have decreased significantly. The rise and fall of the construction industry in this city in recent years, as well as the comparison of timber and cement imports, are described below for reference:

1. Construction in This City

Since this city was opened as a commercial port during the Daoguang period of the Qing Dynasty, it has been vigorously managed by Chinese and foreign people. Commerce and industry have become increasingly prosperous, and the population has increased. As of now, the city's population has reached more than 3.5 million. Therefore, the booming construction industry is to be expected. Taking the total construction amount of the city in the recent eight years as an example, the total annual construction amount of the city in the 16th year of the Republic of China was 15,263,552 taels (silver standard). It gradually increased to 71,511,816 taels (silver standard) in the 19th year of the Republic of China, which is more than 3.67 times the amount in the previous four years. The reason is the sharp increase in population and the investment of real estate developers. This period can be called the golden age. Later, due to natural disasters, man-made disasters, and the impact of the economic downturn, coupled with the outbreak of the January 28 Incident, paradise was regarded as a dangerous place. Some wealthy households moved to the interior, and real estate developers did not dare to invest. Therefore, the city's construction statistics in the 21st year of the Republic of China decreased by more than one digit compared to the 19th year, only 35,541,100 taels (silver standard). As of last year (23rd year), although it did not decrease, it still could not catch up with the huge number in the 19th year. A comparative table of the total number of buildings in the past eight years is shown below:

Year　Total Annual Construction Amount

16　15,263,552 taels

17　32,356,986 taels

18　45,386,682 taels

19　71,511,816 taels

Year　Total Annual Construction Amount

20　62,351,250 taels

21　35,541,009 taels

22　58,268,150 yuan

23　64,112,000 yuan

In recent years, with the bankruptcy of the rural economy, the decline of various industries, and the global economic downturn, the decline in construction volume is also a phenomenon that should be seen. However, it is still able to stand at a total construction volume of more than 64 million yuan each year, an increase of 5,843,850 yuan compared to the previous year, presenting a thriving trend. There are two reasons for this: First, the inland areas are facing continuous disasters and life is difficult. Therefore, people in the inland areas are seeking a way out in the cities. As the population increases in the cities, it is necessary to find accommodation. For example, opening up barren areas and building affordable housing in the Greater Shanghai area, as well as large-scale construction in the city center. Second, the development of high-rise buildings in the concessions. Whether the buildings have been built or not, they are all implementing the principle of occupying the sky but not the land, and actively increasing their height. With these two points, it is appropriate that the construction industry is not declining. Of the total amount of 64,112,000 yuan in the city last year, the public concession accounted for 27,601,000 yuan, followed by the Greater Shanghai area with 23,735,000 yuan, and then the French concession with 12,776,000 yuan. It can be seen that the efforts in building in the Greater Shanghai area are not weak compared to the concessions. Since the construction industry in this city is as described above, the construction factories operating in this industry are naturally very developed. There are currently more than 2,000 factories in the city, of which more than 1,000 have the scale of construction factories. The rest are construction factories that only undertake part of the work, such as decoration, painting, or renovation, woodworking, etc., which are called construction factories. As for those with a larger scope, there are only more than 200 factories.

The Latest Theater Design in the United States (Part 1) 234

— Original by B.A. Hueton, translated by Xiao Ang

The United States is a very wealthy country, and most of its people are rich. Therefore, there are a particularly large number of entertainment venues. According to statistics, there are more than 100 large theaters in New York City, not including the small ones. Although Shanghai's theaters are very developed, I am afraid they are far behind. Recently, due to business competition, the owners of the theaters have gradually paid attention to the form and design of the theater buildings. One theater with the most abundant capital wanted to renovate the theater due to the sluggish business in recent months, so it publicly sought design drawings. The young architect Hueton became famous because of this. His design is indeed precise and thoughtful, worthy of being a genius architect. I am now going to introduce his design very simply, which will definitely be of great help to the architectural community in Shanghai. At the same time, it may also be a considerable encouragement to young architects.

(1) Choice of Location

The theater should be located in an area with convenient transportation and the largest population. The most important thing is to be on the main lines of the city's roads, such as near the Great Road and the French Great Road in Shanghai, which is very suitable. At the same time, the theater should be near the parking lot and the drop-off entrance should be on one side, because too far or having to cross the road will disappoint movie fans. The front of the theater should have a very wide road, because the cars of the ladies and wives will come one after another shortly before the play starts, especially on rest days and when good films are playing. If there is no very wide road, I am afraid there will be accidents. The large theaters in Shanghai do not pay attention to this point and should be improved.

Architectural Jargon (17) 235

— Mei Zhenhuan

—About Use in Construction Sites—

Trowel—The "portable treasure" that a mason cannot leave behind is the trowel and iron plate. The trowel is almost always used when building walls. However, the trowel itself is sometimes used by the mason to represent the measurement of feet as a standard for the number of layers. It is generally calculated based on the length of the trowel (that is, the section of the back of the blade and the handle). Generally, a 2-fen gray joint (detailed previously) is considered one layer, then the length of the trowel is suitable for five layers. Because the first thing to pay attention to when building a wall in a clear water area is the gray joint, so as to avoid the disadvantages of being crooked. The mason then came up with this method.

Iron Plate—Masons must use an iron plate for brushing, whether it is scraping, powdered lime, or fine sand. There is also a kind called steel skin iron plate, which is twice as big as the ordinary one. It is almost indispensable when encountering powdered gypsum. Because the texture of the steel skin iron plate is smooth and clean, powdered gypsum must be fine and smooth, so the ordinary iron plate cannot be used.

Clear Water—The original appearance of the wall surface without brushing any material is called clear water. If it is mixed with cement, lime, fine sand, gypsum, or polished stone, etc., it is collectively called mixed water.

Sprayer—The brick material used for building walls must first be soaked in water. If it is impossible to do so, it must be watered sufficiently. Because the brick material itself is dry, the mason will scrape the sand and mud onto the brick block and build it on the wall without asking why if they do not water or soak it. If it is in a sunny place, it will not be able to withstand the sun and night dew. The wall body that should be used for thirty years will become more than ten years. Therefore, it is necessary to fully irrigate the brick material with water. Supervisors must not be negligent. At the same time, the bricks on the scaffolding are watered on the scaffolding with a sprayer. Therefore, this kind of thing is also indispensable in the construction site.

Crane—In recent years, the construction situation in construction sites is not like before, building two or three-story street houses, etc., thinking that it is a big project. In recent years, there are many tall buildings that reach into the clouds in Shanghai alone that have been completed. However, the construction of this kind of large building mostly uses I-beams as the main material for construction. However, the weight of each I-beam cannot be carried by human power, so the crane car has to be used to help the lack of manpower. As for what the shape of the crane is, it has three legs and a long neck, almost exactly like the shape of a crane, so it is called a crane car. In fact, the translated sound is a crane. Its price is very high, and it is not easy for a small capital construction site to buy.

Property Sign—The section on the ridge of the gable (detailed earlier) (which is commonly known as the fire wall) that rises and drags to the eaves and then steps back level by level to the wall body is called the property sign.

Contract—A contract is a regulation for setting up a project

Washer—If the rotating place of the screw is too long, use a washer to support it. It is a square or round iron piece. In the construction site, it is also called dried tofu.

Shaking Class—The organization of a construction site encompasses the power of the masses. It cannot be successfully achieved by individual authority. Therefore, in the construction site, whether it is the supervisor in the accounting room or the "small business" brought by the workers, all parties should unite and be friendly to each other, unless they take actions outside of the work. It is not allowed to be intimidating. And especially the supervisors in the relief room. Almost everyone has sufficient knowledge and considerable intelligence. They should guide the workers step by step, because the workers do not understand the principles. If the two sides break down, it is easy to feel棘手 and helpless. Sometimes the public anger is aroused, and maybe the whole strike. However, a construction site does not call it a strike, but it is called shaking class. Shaking class is the most taboo thing in a construction site. (To be continued)

Study of Building Materials (Continued) 236

— Zhu Zhenmu

Chapter 9 Lead, Tin, Nickel, Magnesium

Section 1: Lead

Lead is also a sulfide mineral. Its smelting first involves calcination to remove sulfur and convert it into lead oxide. Then, minerals are used to remove oxygen to obtain lead. Lead's color is grayish-white and it is extremely heavy, weighing about 0.41 pounds per cubic inch. It is highly ductile but cannot withstand high compressive forces. Its tensile strength is only 500 pounds per square inch, and the highest is no more than 2,400 pounds. Its use in the construction industry is for various water and electrical distribution pipes.

Section 2: Tin

Tin is an oxide mineral, mostly produced in England. It is ductile and easily fusible. It is used in the construction industry for small items. Its manufacture and refining are the same as other metallic materials, washing, smelting, and polishing are all that is needed.

Section 3: Nickel

Nickel is a silver-white metal. Its ore belongs to sulfides. It is highly ductile and has a strong power. Each square inch can withstand an external force of 160,000,000 pounds. It can be used as stainless various building supplies.

Section 4: Magnesium

Magnesium is a light metal, weaker than aluminum, but its applications are almost the same. Its strength is also considerable.
